Western Rebel Army's Momentum Increases Daily; Madrid Seems Trapped in the Core; Ready to Launch Large-Scale Offensive; Most of the Northwest Provinces Controlled

Madrid: General Franco, the leader of the Spanish rebel army, is now rapidly completing preparations to launch a large-scale offensive on Madrid. At the same time, fierce fighting is taking place on Mallorca, the largest island in the Balearic Islands. The rebel army is eager to seize Palma, the richest port on the island. Due to conflicting accounts from both sides, the true situation on the island is difficult to ascertain. According to the rebel army's radio station in Seville, the government army suffered more than 200 deaths and 600 injuries before retreating. However, officials in Madrid claim that the government army infantry, led by Captain Ballaud, known for his bravery in combat, is making steady progress and will soon subdue the entire island. All British nationals on the island are reportedly safe. The British cruiser "Galatea" is currently stationed there to protect British interests. (Reuters dispatch from the 18th)

Seville: The revolutionary army now claims to have control of the northwestern provinces of the country, but the government troops in Malaga and Antequera in the south are still resisting. The capital city of Madrid is now trapped in the core and is likely to fall soon. (Havas dispatch from the 18th)

Burgos, Spain: Moroccan troops arrived here today and marched through the streets, proving that the northern and southern rebel armies have completely joined forces. General Franco, the commander of the southern rebel army, General Mola, the commander of the northern rebel army, and Cabanellas, the chairman of the military government, discussed adopting new tactics today. General Mola declared that the revolutionary army would soon achieve complete victory. Although the date cannot be determined, the enemy is helpless, and the successive victories of our army are clear evidence of victory. General Franco and the troops under my command have now completely joined forces. (Kuomin Daily dispatch from the 17th)

Irun: The rebel army's army in the northwest launched a general offensive today, covered by naval artillery fire, advancing along the Piedras River toward the coast. After reaching Irun, the infantry dug trenches to besiege the city. (Kuomin Daily dispatch from the 17th)

Moroccan Reinforcements Continuously Cross the Sea; General Mola Personally Inspects

Burgos: A special dispatch from our correspondent reports that the National Military Government and the headquarters of the Northern Army established here by the revolutionary army are about to move to Valladolid (south of Burgos). Troops of Moroccan origin in Spanish Morocco recently crossed the Strait of Gibraltar and arrived in southern Spain. They immediately boarded trains and traveled via Merida to Valladolid. Yesterday afternoon, General Mola, the commander of the Northern Army, personally went there to inspect them. General Mola then gave a speech to the crowd, saying that these troops will soon be sent to the front lines of the Northern Army to assist in the battle. Several more regiments will arrive in the next few days. He concluded that the victory of the revolutionary army is not far away. (Havas dispatch from the 18th)

Fierce Fighting in the North; Rebel Army Fails to Capture Irun; Several Rebel Ships Heavily Bombard

Hendaye, France: The Spanish rebel army in the north has repeatedly attacked the city of Irun, but has failed to capture it. The government army militia has taken the opportunity to prepare everything, destroying a section of the road from Pamplona to Irun, and burying landmines in the remaining section to prevent the rebel army from attacking again. (Havas dispatch from the 18th)

Hendaye, Southern France: According to news received from the border between France and Spain, the Spanish government troops and the revolutionary army are still engaged in fierce fighting today in the area of San Sebastian and Irun in the north. The artillery fire from both sides is extremely fierce. On the revolutionary army's side, the cruiser "España" and the destroyer "Velasco" are heavily bombarding the cities of Irun, San Sebastian, Fuenterrabia, and Pasajes. The artillery of the government army is firing from the Guadalupe Fortress (near Fuenterrabia) at the revolutionary army positions near Villa del Prado. It is reported that the revolutionary army troops have approached the city of Irun, but the government troops in the city are still preparing to resist. As of the time of dispatch, the city has not fallen. Several French aircraft are currently flying over the border between the two countries to monitor the border and prevent it from being violated by the warring countries in Spain. (Havas dispatch from the 17th)

Hendaye, Southern France: The rebel army in the province of Asturias in northwestern Spain is now using the port of Oviedo as its last base. The government army once attacked but failed to recapture it. It has now decided to launch another offensive to eliminate it. According to our correspondent in Guipúzcoa Province, the rebel army warships "España" and "Almirante Cervera" bombed several cities in the north of the province yesterday, namely Irun, San Sebastian, Fuenterrabia, and Pasajes, firing no less than 120 shells. However, none of the shells hit the government army's San Marcos and Guadalupe fortresses. (Havas dispatch from the 18th)

Madrid: The rebel army in northern Spain is determined to seize San Sebastian. Until recently, rebel warships have been heavily bombarding the city, and the Guadalupe Fortress is returning fire. The fighting has continued all night. It is said that there are more than 1,200 political prisoners held in the government army's fortress. To the east of this, the rebel army is advancing towards Irun on the French-Spanish border. The town of Hendaye in France is located north of Irun. Yesterday, residents of Fuenterrabia flocked to the area to take refuge. Some refugees crossed the river when the water was shallow, while others crossed by boat, carrying various items. The government army claims to have occupied the Chijon area of Oviedo. Yesterday, two rebel army leaders, General Fanjul and Colonel Quintana, were executed by firing squad. Fanjul even held a wedding ceremony with his fiancée, Ms. Agueda, before the execution. (Reuters dispatch from the 18th)

Hendaye: The Spanish rebel army warships, unwilling to heed the warning from the government army leader that they would kill all 2,000 prisoners, began to bombard the forts protecting Irun, San Sebastian, and Bilbao today. The "España," sister ship of the "Jaime I," bombed the Guadalupe Fortress. Three other rebel ships fired on other key points. In the evening, the "Cervera" bombarded the city of San Sebastian, firing every ten minutes. The "España" then sailed west. The Guadalupe Fortress is full of landmines, and if it is hit, it will explode, and hundreds of political prisoners held there will be killed. It is said that the Spanish King's advisor, Count Romanones, is also among them. Today, 300 refugees, mostly women and children, crossed the Bidasoa River in small boats or by swimming to escape into French territory. The French authorities have begun an investigation and will protest the Spanish government army's bombing of the border area of Piria d'Arch. The mayor of San Sebastian said that the situation there is dangerous, due to foreign interference and a lack of military supplies. He also denied that the government army had suffered heavy losses, saying that according to his estimate, the government army had suffered 200 deaths and 500 injuries. (Kuomin She dispatch from the 17th)

Comparison of Forces: 500,000 Militiamen Fight the Rebel Army

Madrid: According to general estimates, about 80% of Spain's total military force, totaling more than 235,000 men, have rebelled, and are fighting against more than 500,000 militiamen hastily recruited by the government. With a few exceptions, the newly recruited soldiers are fighting on the front lines so that they can be trained at any time. It is said that as a result of the rebel army's victory in Badajoz, they are now able to communicate directly with the rebel-occupied areas from the French border. The route passes through Pamplona, Burgos, Medina del Campo, Merida, Seville, and Cadiz. However, this route is very time-consuming and dangerous, as it is feared that supporters of the government have blown up many of the bridges along the way. (Reuters dispatch from the 18th)

Revolutionary Army Releases War Report

Burgos: The Revolutionary Army Headquarters released a war bulletin at 10:00 PM last night: (1) In the area of Somosierra and the Guadarrama Mountains (north of Madrid), the government army has been bombarding our army's positions with artillery fire for days, trying to prevent our army from advancing, but the results have been ineffective. (2) In the area of Guipúzcoa and Navarre in the north, after a fierce battle with the government army, our army occupied the city of Andoain and seized countless military supplies. (3) In the province of Asturias, a team of our army is currently besieged in the port of Oviedo. Eight divisions of troops have been sent there to relieve the siege. (4) In the province of Aragon, the government army attacked, but was repelled by our army. (5) In the southern provinces of Córdoba, Granada, and Málaga, the remnants of the government army have been eliminated by our army, and our position has been greatly consolidated. (Havas dispatch from the 18th)

An Observer's Remarks: The Perilous Situation in the Capital; Inferior Weapons Held by Militias

Gibraltar: Today, an experienced observer from Madrid arrived here. According to him, "There are indeed many brave individuals in the Spanish government's militias, the likes of whom I have never seen. However, because the weapons wielded by the militiamen are extremely crude and inferior, they are in a very difficult position. Many militiamen only possess flintlock rifles, and some militiamen even have guns that belong in museum displays, many of which have not been fired for over a century. I personally witnessed a militia unit, composed of both men and women, carrying long-barreled Moorish rifles and advancing to the front lines. We have seen this type of rifle in films about the Foreign Legion. From my observation, the rebels are currently in a position to place Madrid under their control. They are entrenched in the Guadarrama mountains, with ample supplies of munitions and sharpshooters. As for the militias, they are using their ancient, large-caliber short guns to launch continuous attacks, but they have failed to dislodge the rebels. The rebels are merely waiting for reinforcements to arrive, and Madrid could be captured at any time." The observer added that the Spanish government has made various preparations to evacuate three large aircraft currently stationed at the Barajas airfield, seven miles from Madrid. Recently, a rebel aircraft flew over Madrid and dropped a small sandbag on the Puerta del Sol area, with a note attached that read, "This is just a sandbag; it shows how easy it is to drop bombs." Currently, only one train travels eastward from Madrid each day, bringing food into the city. The destination of this train is usually Valencia, but it seems to have recently been changed to Alicante. Judging from the situation, the rebellion in Valencia seems to be more serious than the government admits. The city of Madrid originally planned to cut off electricity supply every night at 11 p.m. to prevent rebel air raids, but this measure has now been canceled because, in the darkness, there have been many incidents of throat-slitting violence every night. The worker's recreation area of Casa de Campo, outside Madrid, has been closed and access prohibited because the bodies of those murdered by terror tactics are largely decomposing, posing a great risk to hygiene. At present, the Red Cross emblem is being freely abused, even to the point where women in nurses' uniforms are carrying rifles, and every Red Cross vehicle is filled with armed soldiers. The militias now completely control Madrid. Most women in the city, including foreign women, dare not wear hats on the street, fearing that they will be falsely accused of being members of the propertied class. Anarchists and communists have threatened that after the rebels occupy the capital, anyone wearing a necktie will be shot on sight. The mansions of Spanish nobles have been widely plundered and confiscated, and most treasures have disappeared. (Reuters, 18th)

Rebel War Strategy: Offensive in Northwest, Defensive in Northeast

(Paris) A military observer here has compiled today's Spanish war news and summarized it, saying that the rebel forces are currently on the offensive in the western province of Extremadura (north of Badajoz) and the northern province of Guipúzcoa (where San Sebastian and Irun are located), while taking a defensive posture in the northeastern city of Saragossa and the Mediterranean island of Majorca. As for the government forces, they are concentrating a large army in the southern region of Andalusia (which includes Córdoba and Granada) in an attempt to attack. In the Guadarrama mountains north of the capital, there was only artillery fire yesterday. Government forces fired tear gas, causing the rebel forces to retreat slightly. Apart from that, the news from that area is quite quiet. According to a message from our correspondent with the rebel forces in Burgos (the seat of the rebel National Government), the government forces in Barcelona attempted to cut off the transportation between the rebel-held cities of Huesca and Saragossa, but they failed. The government forces operating south of Saragossa also failed. After the rebel capture of Badajoz, over two thousand members of the Popular Front have been killed. There are no leftist remnants in the city. Madrid is currently still peaceful. There are rumors that the Cartagena naval base on the Mediterranean coast has joined the rebel forces, but this has not been confirmed. (Havas, 18th)

Virgin Mary Dons White Robes Again

A Touching Tale Amidst the Drums of War

Burgos/Saragossa: In the Saragossa Cathedral, there is a statue of the Virgin Mary, which used to wear a long white silk robe, resembling the uniform of an ancient Spanish army general, with gold-edged green stripes and brocade ribbons on the shoulders. After the late dictator General Rivera came here, this robe was taken off and has remained so for eight years. Now that Saragossa is in the hands of the rebel forces, who are devout Catholics, this famous statue of the Virgin Mary has been re-robed, restoring its former majesty. It is a touching tale amidst the drums of war. (Havas, 18th)

If the Spanish Revolution Succeeds, the Form of Government Will Be Decided by a Public Referendum

Lisbon: Spanish rebel leader General Mola met with guests here today, stating, "I am not a prophet, so I cannot determine whether Madrid will succumb to starvation or surrender under duress. I only hope that the resistance will not last long to avoid unnecessary sacrifices." The General also stated that he supports General Franco's military policy of encirclement, and that the form of government in Spain will be decided by the good people of Spain through a public referendum. (Reuters, 18th)

The People are Holding Fast to Defend Freedom; Ultimate Victory is Assured

Observations of the General Secretary of the French General Confederation of Labor

Le Bourget Airport, France: The General Secretary of the Unified General Confederation of Labor, Mr. Stonehouse, recently flew to Spain with a secretary to discuss matters with the leaders of various parties in the Popular Front. Having completed his mission, he returned here by plane at 6:30 p.m. today. After disembarking, he declared, "The Spanish people are now holding weapons to defend their freedom and rights. Their strength is unparalleled, and victory is assured. Although it may take time, the ultimate victory will surely belong to the people." (Havas, 17th)

Nominee for New Spanish Ambassador to Germany; Dr. Rubió to Succeed

Barcelona: The Spanish Ambassador to Germany, Mr. Cotiho, resigned on the 30th of last month, and his vacancy has now been internally decided to be filled by Dr. Rubió. Dr. Rubió is a renowned archaeologist from the Autonomous Region of Catalonia, who previously studied in Germany and is currently the President of the University of Barcelona. Once the German government expresses its consent, the official announcement can be made. (Havas, 17th)

(Paris) According to the Paris Echo, the military attaché of the Spanish Embassy in France, Major Barroso, resigned from his position last month because of his sympathy for the rebels in his country. He has remained here and has been active since his resignation. The French government has ordered him to leave the country to avoid complications. (Havas, 18th)

Hidden Gold Discovered in Monastery

Completely Confiscated by the Government

Madrid: The local newspapers have prominently featured and sarcastically criticized the discovery by the militias of a vault in a certain monastery, containing 100 million pesetas (Spanish currency), half in cash and the rest in bonds and a large number of gold coins. It is said that the vault was held at a bank in the name of the Poor Clares. The money has now been confiscated. (Reuters, 18th)

Two US Warships Sail to Spanish Waters

(Washington) The State Department announced that the destroyers USS Kane and USS Hatfield were ordered to depart from New York Harbor this afternoon to be stationed in Spanish territorial waters. (Havas, 17th)

Another Proof of Italian Aid to Spanish Rebels

Tangier: Today, diplomatic circles here learned that the Italian cruiser Savoia landed 100 soldiers in Malaga on Thursday to protect the Italian consul there and the son of the rebel General Tranno, who boarded the ship and sailed here to land. It is claimed that the Italian consul had previously helped Tranno escape to Texth, Morocco. Because the government forces in Malaga were dissatisfied with the Italian consul and threatened to harm him, the Italian government took this action. (Guomin, 17th)

Uruguayan Government Proposes Mediation of the Spanish Conflict; Washington's Attitude is Lukewarm

Capital of Argentina: The Uruguayan Foreign Minister, Mr. Espalter, sent a telegram yesterday to the authorities of various American countries, advocating that all American countries should immediately step in to mediate the Spanish civil war so that the war could be ended as soon as possible. After receiving the telegram, the Argentine Foreign Minister, Mr. Saavedra Lamas, declared to the press that the Uruguayan Foreign Minister's initiative was admirable, but he believed that mediation efforts could not be effective until the Spanish rebels were recognized as belligerents. (Havas, 17th)

(Washington) Regarding the Spanish civil war, after the Uruguayan Foreign Minister, Mr. Espalter, suggested yesterday that all American countries should immediately step in to mediate, the State Department here felt quite indifferent. Although the Undersecretary of State, Mr. Phillips, told the Uruguayan Minister, Mr. Richling, that the US government would give careful study to his country's note, semi-official sources believe that the United States does not intend to interfere in the Spanish affairs or any European events. This is because the US presidential election is to be held in November of this year, and it would be dangerous to interfere in the affairs of other countries before the election. The government is naturally unwilling to do so. (Havas, 17th)

The New Anglo-Egyptian Treaty to be Formally Signed at the End of the Month; Egyptian Prime Minister and Delegation to London

Alexandria, Egypt: The negotiations between Britain and Egypt on the new treaty have been concluded. The various provisions have been initialed one after another, and it has been decided to formally sign the treaty in London at the end of this month. Prime Minister Nahas led a delegation from Cairo to here today, boarding the ship Nile to Marseilles, France, and then to London to participate in the signing. (Havas, 17th)

(London) The Egyptian Prime Minister and a portion of the delegation are scheduled to embark this morning from Alexandria. The entire delegation is expected to arrive in London on Sunday. The delegates will be guests of the British government, and the arrangements for their reception are currently being discussed. (Reuters, 17th)

(Cairo) Regarding the matter of the new Anglo-Egyptian treaty in Cairo, the negotiations between the two sides have been going on for a long time, and the various provisions have been initialed one after another. Among them, concerning the abolition of consular jurisdiction, since the two sides reached a compromise, there has been deep concern that the government may also begin to levy taxes on foreign residents in Egypt based on this new treaty. Rumors have started on the stock market as a result, and the market prices of various stocks have fallen. To reassure the public, the Minister of Finance, Mr. Makram, delivered a speech at the stock exchange yesterday, saying that when the Anglo-Egyptian treaty is formally signed and the government has the right to levy taxes on foreigners, it will certainly proceed with the utmost caution. "The great benefits of foreigners investing and establishing businesses in Egypt and cooperating closely with us are something we have always valued. This was true in the past, and it will continue to be true in the future. In short, we will not tolerate the slightest discrimination against foreigners, either in principle or in fact. Outsiders are unaware of this and have expressed some concern about the government's future tax policy, but in fact, based on the new Anglo-Egyptian treaty, there is no reason to have such worries, either in terms of its results or our intentions," he said. (Havas, 18th)

Page 9

Non-Intervention Agreement on Spain; Germany Expresses Conditional Approval; Italy's Demand is Universal Neutrality; Diplomatic Negotiations in Rome are Underway

(Berlin) Germany's acceptance of the French proposal to maintain neutrality on Spanish affairs is subject to the following three conditions: (1) The Spanish authorities must release the German aircraft detained in Madrid. (2) Countries and industries that manufacture war materials and aircraft must not import aircraft or munitions into Spain, including supplies from private sources. (3) The governments concerned must prevent their citizens from volunteering to assist either side in Spain. (Reuters, 18th)

(Berlin) Regarding the French draft non-intervention agreement, the government submitted a reply yesterday expressing its approval, with rumors that it also put forward two reservations: (1) The German aircraft confiscated by the Spanish authorities should be returned immediately. (2) All countries that manufacture and sell munitions should sign the non-intervention agreement, so that even private individuals in those countries would be prohibited from transporting munitions to Spain. This statement was confirmed by an official communiqué from the German news agency, which also said that it was essential for the governments concerned to immediately take measures to prohibit their citizens from enlisting in the warring factions in Spain and assisting them in their operations. (Havas, 18th)

(Rome) The general expectation is that Germany's attachment of certain reservations to non-intervention in Spanish affairs will coincide with Italy's views and be welcomed by the Roman authorities, namely that non-intervention must be complete in order to be effective. Developments in this matter are expected today. (Reuters, 18th)

(Rome) The Foreign Minister, Count Ciano, received the French Ambassador, Mr. de Chambrun, and the British Chargé d'Affaires, Mr. Engram, this afternoon. It is understood that the Italian government has not yet submitted a definite response to the French draft non-intervention agreement on the Spanish civil war. Diplomatic negotiations are still underway. However, political figures predict that the reply is expected soon, and responsible figures say that the Italian government has no intention of deliberately delaying matters. On the contrary, its aim is to quickly establish a universal and complete neutrality agreement. (Neutrality here means recognizing both the Spanish government and the rebels as equal belligerent groups.) Furthermore, Prime Minister Mussolini, who was taking a short break in Rimini, returned to the capital to attend to his duties this afternoon. (Havas, 17th)

(Paris) Regarding the French draft non-intervention agreement, the German government has approved it in principle but has put forward several reservations. Newspapers say that Germany's response is still satisfactory, but they are eager to know the scope of the reservations before commenting. They are also looking forward to Italy's swift response. Regarding this matter, Le Petit Parisien reported that the Italian Foreign Minister, Mr. Ciano, will submit his country's definite response to the French Ambassador, Mr. de Chambrun, today or tomorrow. The right-wing newspapers, commenting on Italy's attitude, believe that the French masses are currently putting increasing pressure on the Blum government, which may suddenly make a rash decision and not be restrained. This is what Italy is deeply worried about. Le Jour mentioned the trip to Spain by the General Secretary of the Unified General Confederation of Labor, Mr. Stonehouse, saying, "We can understand why Italy and Portugal put forward reservations on the non-intervention agreement by looking at Stonehouse's trip." The left-wing newspapers expressed impatience with the hesitation and delay of the democratic countries, and their tireless waiting for other countries to respond. Many said that Germany's reservations would allow it to continue to interfere in the Spanish civil war. Among them, the Communist Party's organ, L'Humanité, stated, "Would our ministers not carefully read the records of the atrocities of burning and killing after the fall of the city of Badajoz in Spain? It must be known that the Spanish rebels are currently being supplied with weapons by fascist countries, while our country does not allow the Spanish Republican government to possess defensive weapons, which is why the city of Badajoz was lost. Does the authorities want this kind of thing to happen again? If our French Republic is willing to be slaughtered and allow peace to suffer a fatal blow, then so be it. Otherwise, we must rise up and break this blockade." (Havas, 18th)

(London) Regarding the French draft non-intervention agreement, the German government submitted a reply yesterday, agreeing to participate, but with several reservations. As for the Italian government, it has not yet made any statement. The Conservative newspapers here are silent and refrain from criticism, while the Liberal newspapers express impatience with Italy's delays. Among them, The News Chronicle stated, "The British and French governments must jointly set a date as the deadline for Italy and Germany to submit satisfactory replies, and they should announce that if they do not reply by the deadline, Britain and France may assist the Spanish government without any restrictions." The Manchester Guardian stated, "The Spanish police recently seized a large number of German documents, all of which were correspondence between the local branches of the German National Socialist Party in Spain and secret orders issued by the Berlin headquarters to the Party's General Office in Barcelona, Spain. These documents prove that the political conspiracies and smuggling activities carried out by the National Socialist Party members in Spain have indeed received the assistance of German officials, especially personnel of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs." (Havas, 18th)

British Government Strongly Supports France; Agreement to be Reached Soon

(London) Foreign Secretary Eden will return to the Foreign Office tomorrow afternoon to resume his duties after a short break in Yorkshire. In the meantime, Sir Halifax is acting as Foreign Secretary. Sir Halifax has been in close contact with Eden on the Spanish situation. The important steps taken by the British government on Saturday were discussed with Eden in advance. These steps by the British government aim to establish a non-intervention agreement on the Spanish civil war as soon as possible. Although the governments of Italy and Germany have both expressed their approval in principle of France's non-intervention proposal, the full text of the agreement has not yet been agreed upon. The British government's attitude towards the agreement was clarified in a statement issued on Saturday. The statement announced that the British and French governments had fully agreed with the full text of France's proposal to ban the shipment of munitions to Spain, which would take effect as soon as notes of approval were received from the governments of Germany, Italy, Portugal, and Russia. The Russian and Portuguese governments have already sent letters of approval, but the Portuguese government has attached reservations. The British government is also exerting efforts in Rome and Berlin to support France's proposal so that the agreement can be established soon. The statement on Saturday also stated that since the outbreak of the Spanish rebellion, the British authorities have never issued licenses allowing the shipment of munitions to Spain. After consulting with various countries, they will also find ways to prohibit civilian aircraft from flying to Spain. The British government's admonition to the British public not to assist either side in the Spanish civil war was welcomed by all newspapers. The news that civilian aircraft flew from Britain to Spain to support both sides of the conflict last week caused great unease, but the government had no way to prevent it. According to today's announcement, the relevant administrative departments are now seeking to ensure that the spirit of Saturday's warning statement is implemented to curb actions that contradict the government's desired goals. The Times said that Britain's actions were indeed clarifying the atmosphere in Europe and making the issue of intervention and non-intervention clearer. It also said that any country that delays the negotiation of a non-intervention agreement, or any country whose actions jeopardize the non-intervention proposal, risks dividing Europe into two opposing camps. (Reuters, 17th)

British Undersecretary of State Visits French Diplomatic Authorities

Informing of the Results of the Talks in Berlin

(Paris) Sir Vansittart, the British Undersecretary of State for Foreign Affairs, visited the Olympic Games in Berlin and took the opportunity to hold talks with the German leader Hitler and other authorities. He left Berlin for France yesterday, intending to rest in the province of Brittany in the west for a few days. He stopped here briefly and was received by the Minister of Foreign Affairs, Mr. Delbos, with the British Ambassador to France, Sir Clerk, also in attendance. During the meeting, Sir Vansittart informed Mr. Delbos of the results of the talks in Berlin and also discussed the situation of concluding a non-intervention agreement. According to official sources, the Spanish government has released all the German pilots who were previously detained, and part of Germany's demands has been met, so the non-intervention issue should be resolved quickly. (Germany's document has already been sent, see separate telegram.) Furthermore, Mr. Delbos also received the Spanish Ambassador, Mr. Albornoz, this afternoon to discuss the Spanish situation. (Havas, 17th)

Hurricane Damage in the Philippines; More Severe Damage in the North

(Manila) At the end of last week, a hurricane struck northern Luzon Island, with no fewer than eleven fatalities. The extent of the damage has not yet been determined. In addition to blowing down many houses, the hurricane also damaged crops, so residents in the affected areas are at risk of hunger. At the height of the storm, the American survey ship Fathomer was blown aground. (Reuters, 18th)

Pacific Institute Discusses the Issue of Safeguarding the Security of the Philippines; Japan Still Holds to the Principle of Maximum Common Naval Limits; British Representative Hopes for the Realization of an Anglo-American Alliance

Yosemite, California, USA: The Pacific Institute discussed the Philippine issue this morning. The Japanese representative declared that Japan had never paid attention to the Philippines and was surprised that there was suddenly a discussion of whether the Filipinos could defend themselves. However, the discussion proceeded as usual. The representatives agreed that the only effective way to protect the Philippines was to sign an international treaty guaranteeing the Philippines' permanent neutrality, but the Philippines itself should also strictly adhere to neutrality. The representatives also believed that naval shipbuilding competition was inevitable, but a naval war between the major powers was definitely impossible. From a specialized military strategy perspective, a Pacific war was definitely impossible, as the US naval power can only reach Pearl Harbor in the Hawaiian Islands, the British naval power is limited to Singapore, and Japan is limited to the area around its home base. The British representative, Mr. Smith, declared to the conference this afternoon that the American recovery policy was disappointing, and that the American isolation policy was temporary or permanent. If it was temporary, then the United States should still actively participate in the international economic recovery movement in the future. The only reason the British hoped for an Anglo-American alliance was that the United States could use its full strength to maintain world peace and jointly restore world prosperity. (Guomin, 17th)

The Yosemite Pacific Conference held a round table conference from the 17th to discuss the international repercussions of the American recovery movement. Representatives from Britain, the United States, and Japan heatedly discussed issues from safeguarding the security of the Philippines to naval issues. Regarding safeguarding the security of the Philippines, Japan was not very concerned. However, on the naval issue, Japan insisted on the so-called principle of maximum common limits and did not make any concessions. (Allied, 17th)

Polish Foreign Policy - Consistently Maintaining the Franco-Polish Alliance - Chief of Staff of the French Army Returns Home

Warsaw - The Chief of Staff of the French Army, General Gamelin, was escorted by the Chief of Staff of the Polish Army, General Stachiewicz, to Krakow last night. This morning, they paid their respects at the tomb of the late Marshal Piłsudski, laying a wreath to express their admiration. Subsequently, General Stachiewicz hosted a luncheon. At 9:25 PM, they departed from the city by car, heading to Vienna and then back to Paris. Before departing, he told people that he was very satisfied to have met with the leaders of the Polish Army and discussed various matters. It is reported that General Gamelin met with Inspector-General of the Army, General Rydz-Śmigły, several times during his visit. It is said that the discussions covered more than one topic, including the impact of Germany's advance into the Rhineland on March 7th on the Franco-Polish defensive alliance. Military sources claim that General Rydz-Śmigły is eager to strengthen Poland's national defense and discussed concrete methods for doing so with General Gamelin at length. Furthermore, it is widely rumored that the Chief of Staff of the Romanian Army, General Sasonovici, will also visit soon. In general opinion, Poland's foreign policy is consistently based on alliances separately established with France and Romania. (Havas, 17th)

Japan's Four Ministers' Conference - Deliberating National Defense Countermeasures

Finance Minister Explains the Current Financial Situation, Requests Understanding from the Military

(Tokyo) Prime Minister Hirota is proceeding smoothly with the preliminary work for deciding national policy, and thus entered the second phase of work. After the cabinet meeting on the 18th, he specially invited Finance Minister Baba and Army Minister Terauchi (Navy Minister Nagano stayed behind briefly). Prime Minister Hirota first explained that the four major guidelines for the decided national policy are: (1) Strengthening national defense, (2) Tax system reform including tax increases, (3) Promotion of industry and trade, and (4) Stabilization of national life. He requested the understanding of the two ministers from the military. Next, Finance Minister Baba explained the outline of the revenue plan, stating that the necessity of strengthening national defense is undeniable, but the reality of the financial situation is dire. Therefore, he hoped that the Army and Navy would consider the current financial situation and assist the financial authorities in smoothly carrying out the decided national policy and compiling the budget, requesting the cooperation of the two ministers. Next, Army Minister Terauchi explained the necessity of the Army strengthening national defense and its general guidelines. Navy Minister Nagano then explained the Navy's plan for strengthening national defense and the outline of the budget for the next fiscal year. Finally, they exchanged opinions regarding the specific issues of sourcing funds and deciding national policy, and then adjourned. (Domei, 18th)

Northeast Anti-Japanese Volunteers Active - Zhao Shangzhi's Troops Attack Yilan County, Fierce Battle, Japanese Troops Retreat

(Harbin) More than 100 soldiers from the Northeast Anti-Japanese Volunteer Army led by Zhao Shangzhi attacked Yilan County at approximately 5:00 AM this morning, engaging in a fierce battle with Japanese troops, various units, and mixed puppet troops for over an hour. It is said that the Volunteer Army captured a large amount of firearms and ammunition. (Hualian, 18th)

(Tokyo) After Governor-General of Taiwan, Nakagawa, submitted his resignation, the government authorities were extremely cautious in selecting a successor. Japanese Immigrants to Brazil - Over Five Hundred People Departed Kobe Yesterday

Kobe - Eight hundred and eighty-eight Japanese immigrants from eighty families departed Kobe at 4:00 PM on the 18th aboard the merchant ship "Montevideo Maru" bound for Brazil, the new world. (Domei, 18th)

Development of Japan's Shipbuilding Industry - Seven Hundred Thousand Tons Under Construction

(Tokyo) Recently, all large and small shipyards in Japan have been very busy due to the prosperous state of the shipbuilding industry. The total tonnage of ships under construction and nearing completion in various shipyards is approximately 700,000 tons or more. From the most depressed period of the shipbuilding industry in Showa 7 (1932) to the present, in the past four years, excluding ships under 1,000 tons, a total of 70 ships totaling 397,946 tons have been newly built. This demonstrates the astonishing achievements of Japan's shipbuilding industry in a short period of time. The ships built in the past four years can be categorized by ship type as follows: 14 small ships under 4,000 tons, 22 medium-sized ships between 4,000 and 7,000 tons, 21 large ships between 7,000 and 10,000 tons, and 14 ships over 10,000 tons. The annual increase in large and excellent cargo ships is particularly noteworthy. Furthermore, during these four years, the government has protected and subsidized the improvement of shipbuilding facilities in three phases. During this time, a total of 119 old ships totaling 499,000 tons were scrapped, indicating that many obsolete and aging ships have been phased out. (Domei, 18th)

Canada - Quebec Provincial Election - National Union Party Wins Big

Quebec, Canada - The Quebec Liberal Party, which has held power for 39 years, has failed in today's election. The National Union Party won a major victory, securing 76 seats while the Liberal Party only won 14 seats. It is said that the provincial government will be reorganized after the election results are announced. The election is not yet completely over and competition is fierce. It is rumored that the National Union Party previously advocated Quebec's withdrawal from the Canadian Dominion government and the British Empire, but the party leader Duplessis denies this claim. (National News Agency, 17th)

Turkey Withdraws Diplomatic Missions from Addis Ababa

Ethiopian Prince Travels to Holy Land Via Britain and France

International Commercial Telegram

August 18th, Reuters Special Business Report

Gold and Silver

London Gold Price: Today fell one penny to 138 shillings and fourpence.

London Silver: The market is stable today. Spot and forward prices are both 19 pence 4375, each down 0.0625. There is slight demand from American counterparts, India sold.

Oath-Taking Ceremony for Guangdong Officials - Original Speech of Chairman Chiang

The newly appointed Guangdong party, government, and military officials held an oath-taking ceremony on the morning of the 17th. Chairman Chiang, representing the Central Committee, personally supervised the oath-taking and delivered a speech. The original speech is as follows: "Comrades, today we, the Guangdong party affairs, political, and military committee comrades, are jointly taking the oath of office at the Sun Yat-sen Memorial Hall. I, Zhongzheng, under the command of the Central Committee, am personally here to supervise the oath-taking and participate in this grand ceremony. To meet with so many comrades who have been apart for ten years reminds me of the various things from ten years ago, like a traveler returning home, with indescribable emotions. As you all know, today's grand gathering is a memorial to the revolutionary base regaining the true leadership of our party. It is the result of Commander Yu leading the army, navy, and air force soldiers and comrades through all kinds of hardships to correct the chaos and reverse the wrong. It is also the starting point for our future efforts to create a unified China. It is truly a very rare grand gathering. I, Zhongzheng, would like to take this opportunity to share my thoughts, our hopes for the party, government, and military in the future, and how we should strive to achieve them. First of all, I can say that Guangdong is not only Guangdong of China but also Guangdong of the Chinese Kuomintang. Guangdong has an inseparable relationship with the Chinese National Revolution. Our late Premier spent his entire revolutionary life of forty years basing himself solely in Guangdong. Before the establishment of the Republic of China, he fought against the Manchurian Qing government. After the founding of the Republic, he fought bitterly against rebels and separatist warlords. During that time, he endured countless hardships, dangers, and pain. Unfortunately, after the reorganization of our party in the thirteenth year of the Republic, in the fourteenth year, the Premier departed us and passed away. In the years before the Premier's death, Guangdong was in a state of disarray due to separatism and division. Countless warlords controlled the finances and provincial government. Armies from various provinces treated Guangdong as a territory to be arbitrarily divided, reducing the people to abject poverty. The people of Guangdong could not distinguish whether this was a revolution or warlordism. These rebels and warlords completely disregarded the Premier's orders, only asking the Premier for funds and weapons, making various demands, even making unreasonable demands and plotting wrongdoings. The Premier always maintained a forgiving attitude and painstakingly maintained this revolutionary base, but his inner pain deepened day by day, and he soon passed away. I, Zhongzheng, always believed that 'if the situation in Guangdong is not unified, the revolution will be unable to progress. If Guangdong is unified, the unification of China will not be a problem.' Since the fourteenth year, under the command of our party, I and other comrades, especially leading armed comrades, spent two years of hard work to eliminate the rebels and warlords entrenched in Guangdong, unifying the divided Guangdong, returning the interests of Guangdong to the people of Guangdong, and handing over the entire revolutionary base to the central government of our party. Only then did the revolution have a foundation, and we could wholeheartedly proceed with the Northern Expedition. Since leaving Guangdong, ten years have passed in a flash. Because I, Zhongzheng, was focused on launching the Northern Expedition, I did not properly organize the military and party affairs, did not firmly establish the revolutionary foundation, did not fully instill the bright path of revolution and the fundamental spirit into successors, nor did I pass on the methods of implementing the Three Principles of the People to the comrades left behind, so that they could carry them out to the end in accordance with the revolutionary spirit. As a result, in the past ten years, chaos has occurred repeatedly. Although the revolutionary progress of the whole country has gone further, the suffering of the revolutionary base has also deepened. Party affairs disputes, political oppression, not only have the people suffered, the party members have suffered, especially making many overseas Chinese suffer all kinds of pain. During these ten years, it was impossible for our true revolutionaries to even come to Guangdong. The revolutionary achievements were almost completely destroyed. The entire revolutionary foundation was almost overturned. This is certainly due to the successors not knowing how to conduct themselves and continuously going down the wrong path. But I, Zhongzheng, in self-reflection, believe that it is always due to my lack of morality and credibility. I am truly sorry to the Premier, sorry to my comrades-in-arms, and especially sorry to the people of Guangdong who have supported the revolution and made the greatest sacrifices. Now, fortunately, Commander Yu and the officers and soldiers have deeply understood the righteousness, corrected the chaos, and reversed the wrong, uniting to restore the revolutionary base, restoring Guangdong's glorious position in history. Looking back on the suffering of the past ten years, today our revolutionary officers, soldiers, and comrades can all gather together, distinguishing the true revolutionaries from the fake revolutionaries. Looking back on the past, I am truly filled with grief and shame, beyond words. Comrades, you must know that this undertaking of correcting the chaos and reversing the wrong is not easy. It is due to Commander Yu and the army, navy, and air force officers and soldiers, especially the air force comrades, in extremely difficult circumstances, holding firm to their revolutionary faith, recognizing the position of the nation and the people, upholding justice, distinguishing public and private, and struggling through hardships. This spirit of great benevolence, great courage, utmost impartiality, and utmost loyalty has swept away the obstacles of the past ten years in one stroke. Everyone must know that this is a very difficult thing. Only those who know only the country, not themselves, who know only the revolution, not rights, can do it. In particular, Commander Yu and the officers and soldiers have demonstrated public-mindedness, loyalty, and patriotism, sacrificing their positions, and can truly serve as a model for revolutionary soldiers. This time, we were able to recover Guangdong, this revolutionary base, and unify it under the command of the Central Committee. This is certainly due to the determination and struggle of many comrades and generals, but Commander Yu's spirit of loyalty to the party and the country is especially worthy of our admiration. Even this time, before he returned to Guangdong from Nanjing, I, Zhongzheng, sincerely asked him, "The Central Committee fully knows that you are a revolutionary. In order for you to thoroughly assume the responsibility of reorganizing Guangdong, I want to completely hand over the military and political affairs to you, so that you can take charge and be responsible. I hope you will take charge of the military and civil administration as a whole, and follow the orders and discipline of the Central Committee to create a model province." Commander Yu then said, "I can fully assume the military affairs and work together with my fellow countrymen. However, I am truly not capable of political affairs and must ask the Central Committee to appoint capable and virtuous people to take up the positions in the provincial government." This humble, selfless, and upright spirit is truly worthy of being a model for modern revolutionary soldiers. From this, it can be further known that our Guangdong officers and soldiers reversed the wrong this time entirely out of a revolutionary standpoint. Commander Yu thoroughly demands unification, hoping that the Central Committee can fundamentally transform and consolidate Guangdong, this important revolutionary base, in order to complete the great cause of national revival. With this spirit of his, coupled with the fact that all the revolutionary officers and soldiers in Guangdong can automatically abandon the positions of army commander, division commander, and brigade commander, opening a new epoch unprecedented for revolutionary soldiers since the founding of the Republic of China, this great and memorable event has truly added infinite hope and strength to the country. I further hope that the civil and military comrades who assist Commander Yu will all understand his open-minded, selfless, and public-spiritedness, assist him in achieving his virtues, and implement his cause. If we are truly revolutionary, we must always take the success or failure of the ideology and the misfortunes of the nation as the premise, and not take personal interests and gains as the center. Do not only consider the immediate interests, but establish a solid and unshakeable foundation for the country for all future generations. We must ensure that the old and backward ideas of narrow-mindedness, selfishness, or separation of factions and boundaries are completely eradicated in the new Guangdong after unification. Our comrades in the party, government, and military must know how the compatriots across the country are paying attention to Guangdong's future facilities and development, and how the people of Guangdong are expecting the implementation of our Three Principles of the People and the emergence of a new politics. In this once-in-a-lifetime opportunity, to comfort the compatriots across the country and the expectations of the people of Guangdong, the most important thing is that the party, government, and military must be completely united, working together with one heart to make efforts. It is not good to be like before. Now, the party headquarters, government, and army must all fulfill their responsibilities and jointly promote the progress, creating benefits for the society and the people, so that they can be worthy of being the source of the revolution. The army, party headquarters, and government must all be like this. There must be a close connection between the three, proceeding towards one goal, and must have a close relationship with the actual interests of society and the people. Everyone must take this opportunity to work together to lay a very solid and complete foundation, creating a model province for realizing the Three Principles of the People, comforting the suffering people, refreshing the politics of Guangdong, reversing the declining customs of the past, and completing the great cause. (To be continued)"

Amidst Mediation of Guangxi Affairs, Guangxi Province is Filled with Wartime Atmosphere, Waterway Traffic on the Upper Guijiang River is Cut Off

Guangzhou Correspondence: Regarding the Guangxi issue, according to returning guests from Guangxi, the attitude of the generals of Guangxi towards peace and war still shifts with the attitude of Li Bai. The elite troops of the Guangxi army are distributed in the northeast of Guangxi, with new recruits defending the rest. As for the defense situation, the entire province is divided into four war zones. The area around Yongzhou and Liuzhou is the base, with the three divisions of Liao Lei's troops deployed separately. The area around northern Guangxi, from Guilin and Quanzhou to Hexian County, is defended by the three divisions of Wang Zanbin's troops. Wuzhou up to Pingnan and Tengxian County is garrisoned by the 19th Division of Zhou Zuhuang's division and artillery. New recruits have been arriving continuously in recent days, numbering no less than 8,000. It is reported that the first division of the Guangxi Provincial Defense Self-Defense Army, led by Xu Qiming, and the second division, led by Lin Cixi, have been dispatched from Hengxian County to Nanxiang, spying on the Qinzhou and Lianzhou areas on the border of Guangdong. It is rumored that the vanguard arrived in Lianzhou City on the 9th of this month. The third division of the Guangxi Provincial Defense Army, led by Zhang Jian, with approximately 5,000 men, advanced to Nachenxu on the 8th, appearing as if to enter Qinzhou. At present, the entire Guangxi is filled with a wartime atmosphere. The waterways above Wuzhou have been closed, and major rivers are filled with mines. The troops travel back and forth on temporary pontoon bridges, which will be demolished immediately if necessary. A garrison command has been established in Yulin to command the militia. In the event of an outbreak of war, a scorched-earth policy will be implemented. The people are being trained daily to evacuate and practice air defense drills. The Wuzhou Hospital is stepping up the organization of four temporary ambulance teams and one stretcher team. The Wuzhou Hospital has now been converted into the rear hospital of the Fourth Army Group. It is also reported that due to the concentration of large troops in eastern Guangxi, traffic on the upper river has been cut off since the 4th of this month. The people of Guangxi are moving away one after another, and the scene is as if a great war is about to break out at any moment. (August 15th)

Xiamen: Japanese Consulate Arbitrarily Arrests Chinese, Detaining and Torturing for Ten Days

Xiamen Correspondence: Ji Maolin, an inspector of the former Xiamen Kerosene Tax Bureau and Sugar Tax Bureau, was arrested by three Japanese policemen from the Xiamen branch of the Japanese Police at 10:00 AM on August 4th on the second floor of the Lu Kun Restaurant on Siming South Road. He was immediately taken to the Japanese Consulate on Gulangyu Island and detained until 4:00 PM on the 14th before being released. Ji is from Houshe Village, Tong'an. The Japanese Consulate insisted that he was a Taiwanese man nicknamed "Dwarf Lin from Taiwan." According to a complaint made by Taiwanese people to the Japanese Consulate, "Dwarf Lin" had allegedly beaten Taiwanese people, hence the arrest. Ji told people after his release that his arrest was actually due to his seizure of smuggled white sugar during his previous tenure as an inspector, which led to enemies reporting him to the Japanese Consulate. On the day he was taken to the Japanese Consulate, Japanese policemen presented torture instruments such as lead hammers, chisels, and wooden implements, forcing him to admit he was Taiwanese. Despite enduring physical torture, Ji firmly refused to admit it and provided proof of his origins from Houshe Village, Tong'an, including his parents and family. After the interrogation, he was detained in the consulate's prison for investigation. Later, after it was confirmed that he was indeed not from Taiwan, they harshly questioned him about the beating of Taiwanese people. Ji strongly denied it and was finally released on the 14th. Ji believes that the Japanese Consulate exceeded its authority by arbitrarily detaining and torturing him and has submitted a petition to the Municipal Government to negotiate with the Japanese Consulate. According to the Japanese Police Station's branch in Xiamen (the main station is in the Consulate on Gulangyu), before the September 18th Incident, they resided in Xiamen in the manner of Japanese Consulate staff living at home. Nowadays, when arresting Chinese citizens, the Japanese Consulate would send consulate staff to request our officials to make the arrest and then extradite them. After the September 18th Incident, its branch began to independently exercise its police powers in Xiamen, directly arresting its citizens within our territory without consulting or notifying our officials. This case of Ji Maolin is the first instance of arresting our citizens within our territory and detaining them in the consulate's prison for torture for as long as ten days in Xiamen. (August 16th)

Over a Hundred Guangdong Business Groups Appeal for the Abolition of Harsh Taxes and Levies; Over Forty Shantou Business Guilds Reiterate Their Appeal; Over Sixty Guangzhou Merchant Guilds Prepare to Petition

Guangzhou Correspondence: Guangdong Province's harsh taxes and levies are the most severe in the country. In recent years, whenever Guangdong Province introduces a new policy, the expenses are always covered by new taxes and levies. Moreover, the number of troops is particularly large, and military expenditures are enormous, resulting in a situation where miscellaneous taxes are piled upon each other, making it impossible to abolish them. Recently, the central government issued a clear order to abolish Guangdong's harsh taxes, giving the people of Guangdong hope like rain after a long drought. The Department of Finance is currently reviewing and implementing this policy. To ensure that the Department of Finance can abolish the harsh taxes as soon as possible, the silk and cloth industry, fertilizer industry, cotton yarn industry, match industry, dye industry, rice industry, industry, remittance industry, Chinese medicine industry, silver industry, theater industry, travel industry, vegetable industry, restaurant industry, firewood and charcoal industry, shoe industry, oil pressing industry, domestically produced kerosene industry, prepared medicine industry, Western medicine industry, oil industry, brown sugar industry, ceramics industry, fresh fish industry, and fruit industry, among more than forty guilds in Shantou, have again sent telegrams requesting the swift abolition of harsh taxes and levies, stating roughly that the guilds, etc., have been under oppressive and exorbitant taxation, with all the burdens of harsh taxes and levies being heavily exploited, causing deep pain, with some items being taxed twice or being levies not authorized by central government policies. Now that political affairs are clear, they humbly request that the harsh taxes and levies that various guilds in Shantou telegraphed to be abolished some days ago be abolished by clear order, so that they can enjoy benevolent governance and its benefits. Furthermore, in Guangzhou, the most prominent and obvious harsh and miscellaneous taxes include the advertisement tax, the surcharge for maintaining paper currency, the business tax on the film industry, theater taxes, the leather tax on the leather shoe material industry, the national defense surcharge, the fees for operating public buses, license fees, permit fees, various raw material taxes on the match industry, the medicinal herb and seafood taxes on the north-south brokerage industry, the surcharges and verification fees on the metal industry, the agricultural tax, foreign paper special tax, joss paper tax, incense and candle tax on the paper industry, the sesame and bean tax on the miscellaneous grain industry, the special tax on goods imported from other provinces, the surcharge for Zhongda University, the foreign rice tax on the rice industry, and the liquor license tax on lower-class restaurants, as well as the sugar monopoly tax, which resembles a monopoly. These numerous items cause great harassment to merchants, leading to the increasing decline of commerce. Yesterday, the match industry, metal mining industry, rice industry, miscellaneous grain industry, firewood and charcoal industry, public bus industry, film theater industry, leather shoe material industry, tobacco industry, north-south brokerage industry, paper industry, salted fish industry, Chinese and foreign sundry goods industry, machine-woven shirt and sock industry, native cloth industry, rubber industry, biscuit industry, steamer miscellaneous industry, hotel industry, pigsty industry, cigarette industry and other sixty-odd groups, each sent representatives to hold a joint meeting on the 10th to discuss requesting the abolition of the above-mentioned harsh taxes and levies, listing the painful situation of harsh taxes and miscellaneous levies suffered in Guangzhou, and separately submitted them to the competent authorities, requesting the abolition of the harsh taxes by a set date, and jointly elected representatives to petition on a large scale at a fixed time.
