Songjiang

Robbery Case in Punan

Wu Jinzhang's family, a farmer in Nantang Village, Caojing Township, Eighth District of the county, had some savings, which were coveted by bandits. As expected, at 2:00 AM on the 15th, eight bandits speaking mixed dialects, each holding box guns and wooden clubs, broke into the house through the back door and searched and looted separately. After half an hour, they fled with the stolen goods. The victim has already checked the lost items, prepared a list of losses, and reported it to the responsible police station for investigation. Furthermore, Hu Tu, the first squad leader of the first team of the first district of the Water Police of the province, captured Zhu Zhangfu, also known as Xiao Lao Zhu, a suspected robber from the robbery of Fahua Bridge Town, in Sanbao Liujia Wuhu Village, Mijīng Town, the other day, who is highly suspected of involvement in a major case. He was immediately escorted to the team headquarters and transferred to the District Court Prosecutor's Office for investigation. It was then found that the crime scene was in Fengxian County, and court police Zhou Qiaosheng and Lü Qingchang were immediately dispatched to escort the suspect by car at 11:00 AM to Fengxian for legal proceedings.

Nanhui

Robbery and Assault in the Second District

Lu Yousheng's family, a farmer in Gaoqiao Township, Second District, was suddenly visited by more than ten bandits on the evening of the 15th. They broke open the back door and entered, first tying up Yousheng and his wife with ropes and covering their heads and faces with jackets. When Yousheng cried for help, he was stabbed in the head with a sharp knife, causing him to bleed and faint. They then robbed forty pieces of homespun cloth, thirty quilts, as well as gold jewelry and clothing, causing very heavy losses. It is reported that the robbery lasted for two hours before they fled west with the stolen goods.

Wuxi

Petition Against Police Reduction Causes Great Disturbance

Zhang Da, the new director of the Wuxi County Public Security Bureau, was ordered to come to Wuxi to implement the police district system and was transferred 184 police officers from the province, who were assigned to serve in various sub-bureaus in the urban area. In addition, from the original police officers in the six sub-bureaus in the urban area, he separately examined and selected 184 officers with excellent performance to send to the province for training. Unexpectedly, most of the police officers were unwilling to go to the province for training and appealed to all parties, requesting that they be paid and dismissed to return to their hometowns. At around 9:00 PM the night before, the police officers of the Third Sub-bureau in Nanmen first united with the others and disarmed, entered the West City Gate, and petitioned the County Party Headquarters. At that time, Director Zhang was patrolling on a bicycle when he met the petitioning police officers and was invited to the County Party Headquarters. The police officers appointed Yang Yaowu and five others as representatives to state their petition to Director Zhang: (1) The police officers had already received training and were unwilling to go to the province for training again; (2) They voluntarily resigned en masse and requested that they be paid three months' grace pay, following the Kunshan precedent, so that they could return to their hometowns and be good citizens. Director Zhang earnestly persuaded the petitioning police officers and said, "If I let you down, I will be shot to death by bandits in the future." While he was explaining, more than 100 newly graduated police officers sent by the province suddenly arrived running in formation, causing a tense situation. The petitioning police officers were terrified and fled in all directions. Director Zhang also took refuge in the Party Headquarters. The residents on both sides were also frightened and did not know what to do. At this point, Director Zhang suffered extreme mental stimulation and suddenly fainted. He was revived by the bureau's doctor, Xu Fenghua, and immediately said, "I am sorry to the people of Wuxi for this petition event of the old police officers. I am determined to telegraph Director Yu to request resignation and ask County Chief Long to punish me." County Chief Long had already learned of the above situation and immediately dispatched the entire defense corps to maintain order. At 2:30 AM yesterday morning, the police officers returned to the County Government to await instructions from County Chief Long and raised three points in their petition: (1) The police officers' salaries would be paid up to the 18th, and there would be no rations after the 18th; (2) The old dormitories were already occupied by the new police officers, and the police officers had nowhere to live; (3) They requested that three months' grace pay be given so that they could return to their hometowns and make a living. County Chief Long, after discussing with Duan Qishan, the former chief of the Sixth Sub-bureau, ordered the police officers to temporarily reside in Xifu Temple. As for the rations and grace pay, the method would be determined after reporting to the province. At this point, the police officers dispersed to Xifu Temple to stay temporarily. At 11:00 AM, the County Government had already received an order from the Department of Civil Affairs that the police officers who had already been trained did not need to go to the province again, and the dismissed police officers could be assigned to various counties for placement. However, the police officers were still unable to agree, so they continued to petition various agencies such as the Chamber of Commerce in the afternoon.

Changzhou

Quarrel Over Firewood Leads to Murder

Yin Faxiang, a farmer from Jiaoxi Town, Fifth District of Wuyi, was poor. His grandmother was in charge of guarding a temple on Shun Mountain. Recently, the firewood and grass on the mountain were lush, so his grandmother ordered Faxiang to go up the mountain to collect firewood for fuel. On the 13th of this month, Faxiang went to the mountain. Just as he was collecting firewood, Wu Caigen, a villager, came out to stop him, which led to a fight between the two. Caigen was accidentally pushed by Faxiang and his head hit a mountain rock, causing a hole. They each returned home. However, Caigen was unwilling to submit and often gathered a group of twenty or so young men to Faxiang's residence, dragged him out, and beat him severely before leading the crowd back. Faxiang was seriously injured and died at around 3:00 AM on the 17th after ineffective treatment. Yin Faxiang's mother, Lü, who depended on him for her livelihood, was heartbroken and immediately prepared Baozhang Lu Haoquan to report the case to the District Court. On the 18th, Prosecutor Lü was dispatched to the village to conduct an autopsy and further arrest the murderer for investigation.

Nanjing

Jinpu Railway Bureau Accused of Not Paying Advances

Qiu Runchu, the agent of the former Jinpu Railway catering service Ping Shen Company, accused the Jinpu Railway Bureau of owing more than 50,000 yuan in advances. The case was opened for trial in the Civil Court of the Capital District Court on the morning of August 17th. Jinpu Railway's representative lawyer, Di Kan, argued. As a result of the debate, the judge ordered Ping Shen Company to send the complete monthly business reports submitted to the railway to the court for detailed copying. The case was adjourned for continued hearing on the morning of August 28th.

Gaoyou

Four Families Robbed in Chenyuzui

In Chenyuzui, this county, at about 8:00 PM on the 14th, a bandit ship suddenly arrived with fourteen or fifteen bandits, three of whom had box guns. After landing, they first went to Chen Ruisen's house and looted it clean. Still not satisfied, they hung Chen's wife up and beat her severely, and burned her armpits and legs with kerosene, causing extremely severe injuries. They then went to the homes of Chen Ruiyi, Chen Yishu, and Chen Bikun, and looted them extensively. All the families' cash, totaling about 300 yuan, as well as clothing, jewelry, rice, and grain, were robbed clean, and a large boat was robbed to load the stolen goods. They left after an hour. The total losses of the four families were over a thousand yuan.

Old Monk Hangs Himself

Wuming, the abbot of Changsheng Convent in the Yuecheng Guandi Temple in the north gate of this city, was 56 years old and from Huaicheng. Recently, he was afraid of being sued for something and suddenly had a short-sighted idea and hanged himself in his upstairs room at about 1:00 AM on the 14th. At about 9:00 AM on the morning of the 15th, his disciple, Miancheng, discovered that he had been dead for a long time, so he reported to the Buddhist Association and reported to the county government. At about 5:00 PM in the afternoon, the county government sent Yu Yunhu, the director of the First Branch of the Public Security Bureau, to conduct an autopsy with the coroner, which confirmed the death. He was ordered to prepare a coffin for burial.

Haizhou

Farmers Destroy Township Office

Hu Xingzhao, a farmer from the Third Bao of Jielu Township, Sixth District of Ganyu County, and his nephew Hu Weiyi, Xiang Yanyue and Lin Yuyan, farmers from the Second Bao, Wang Weiru, a farmer from the First Bao, and Chen Wanxiang, a farmer from the Fourth Bao, suddenly went to the Township Office at 6:00 PM yesterday when Township Head Hu was out, opened the door lock, broke into the room, tore up all the official documents and account books, threw them on the ground, and took away an ink box, a stamp, a private seal, and smashed a teapot. After Township Head Hu Jinzhang returned to the office and witnessed the destruction, he filed a report to the county government. After the county government submitted the report, it immediately dispatched a police team to arrest Hu Zhaoxing and others for legal action.

Dinghai

Huge Quantity of Opium Seized

The First Battalion of the Dinghai Water Police sent personnel to inspect the Daxing Wheel when it arrived in Dinghai from Shanghai the other day. They found three pieces of "Daxian Fruit" in the second hold. They instructed the sailors to open them and ordered the police to search. A large package of opium, totaling seventy-four small packages, weighing six catties and nine taels, was found in one of the baskets. When the inspection was being carried out, the owner, Wang Yueqing, looked flustered. After the discovery, he denied that the item belonged to him. The ship's purser, Zhuo Shiting, and the first mate, Xu Baosheng, came forward to testify, and Wang finally confessed. During the inquiry, four large packages of red-lined paper fell from the three Taige onto the sea surface. The inspecting police knew that something was wrong and ordered the sampan to retrieve and dismantle them. They were also opium, weighing up to twenty catties. Due to the large number of passengers, they did not investigate deeply. They then took Wang Yueqing and a suspected sailor to the team for interrogation. Considering the seriousness of the case, the witnesses were also sent to the county for interrogation.

Japanese in Beiping

(Special Dispatch from Beiping)

The number of Japanese residents in North China has now reached more than 19,000 (including Koreans). Among them, those residing in Beiping must be around several thousand. In addition, there are embassy staff and their families, garrison troops, prostitutes, and vagrants whose origins cannot be traced. In general, the number of Japanese in Beiping must reach five or six thousand. These Japanese people are no different from our people in appearance, and sometimes they wear Western clothes or are ashamed to wear Chinese gowns, so it is often difficult to distinguish them from our people. However, under normal circumstances, their legs seem to be slightly shorter than those of our people. As for the few exceptions, one would never know they were Japanese until they opened their mouths. However, there are also those who speak our national language very fluently. Among all the Japanese in Beiping, the most noticeable are the garrison troops. These garrison troops often go out in groups of three or five, or even in entire teams, fully armed, patrolling back and forth in the market and Wangfujing Street. They all wear red armbands and yellow uniforms, and their faces are ruddy and their shoulders are broad, completely different from our country's troops, who wear gray uniforms and are thin and weak. However, compared with the garrison troops of the embassies of European and American countries, they are not only not as majestic in stature, but also their uniforms feel wrinkled and not as straight. When the Japanese army marches, they shout loudly along the way, as if there is no one else around. During the winter vacation last year, they openly teased women in the crowd in the Dong'an Market, which aroused great resentment among our people for a time. When the tanks paraded in the city of Ping last month, they also beat American journalists and destroyed their cameras. Later, they apologized and compensated for the matter. Their arrogance can be seen from this.

The next most noticeable are the vagrants. In addition to running various illegal businesses, these Japanese and Korean vagrants often form gangs and go to public places such as parks, movie theaters, and markets, loitering around, laughing or singing. Their clothes are also extremely untidy. Some wear very elaborate Western-style tops but short, dirty linen pants, while others wear Chinese gowns but wooden clogs and ride bicycles around the streets. The strange shapes are endless. Sometimes they cause trouble in brothels, causing an uproar throughout the city. Most of them are vagrants. A reporter once witnessed four or five vagrants surrounding and hitting the head of a Chinese child in a park. The child cried in pain, while the vagrants laughed loudly and continued to hit him without stopping, taking pleasure in it.

The illegal businesses run by vagrants include the following: (1) trafficking in silver, (2) trafficking in copper coins, (3) trafficking in smuggled goods, (4) running opium dens, (5) running gambling dens, (6) running dance halls. Before our country implemented currency reform last year, these vagrants openly used suitcases and willow bags to forcibly transport silver out of the pass in bundles and piles. Our police and constabulary could do nothing about it. At that time, one silver dollar in Beiping could be exchanged for one dollar and two cents in paper money, which shows the instability of the financial situation. Since our country's currency reform and the nationalization of silver, these vagrants have changed their business to transporting copper coins. For a time, copper coins were in great shortage in the market, and the face value of copper coin notes was very different from the actual exchange price of copper coins, so the prices of daily necessities fluctuated greatly, and small and medium-sized citizens were greatly affected. This year, smuggled goods are more profitable, so these vagrants have turned to running smuggled goods, traveling back and forth on the Pingjin Road and the Pingtong Road, causing smuggled goods to pile up in Beiping. All of this is done by these vagrants. They have an office in the Ruijin Building at the west entrance of Gong'an Street, east of Jiaomin Lane. There are six large characters outside the door: "International Transportation Company." Now the business of smuggling goods is coming to an end, and there is no profit to be made. I don't know what new tricks they will come up with. In addition to the above three types, there are three types of businesses that they run regularly. The first is opium dens. Since the promulgation of the Provisional Regulations for Punishing Crimes Involving Severe Drugs, strict laws have been enacted to punish drug traffickers, drug manufacturers, and drug users. Up until recently, the opium dens opened by Chinese people can be said to have been completely eradicated. If it were not for Japanese and Korean vagrants openly selling drugs, even if one wanted to use drugs, there would be no way to buy them, and the drug atmosphere could be reduced slightly. Unfortunately, they openly opened opium dens, and the Chinese military and police could do nothing about it except for a few that could be searched and confiscated. In addition, there are the gambling dens. In the gambling dens, opium, gambling, and prostitutes are all available. The Beijing Hotel on Meishi Street outside Qianmen is the most prominent of these. Since the spring of this year, they have discovered another thing that can make them a lot of money, and that is opening dance halls. In addition to the Jinshan Dance Hall on Gong'an Street, in June, they opened a White House Dance Hall on Dongchang'an Street with a capital of 100,000 yuan. It has dozens of dancers from Japan, Korea, Russia, and China. The manager is Dr. Kim Tong-guk, a Korean doctor. This dance hall is the largest in this area. Recently, some vagrants have also been engaged in kidnapping. Fortunately, the kidnapping of Madam Zhu Shaoyang was solved quickly, which made them shudder. Otherwise, the hidden dangers would be unthinkable.

Among the vagrants, the Koreans are the most fierce and unreasonable, but they are docile and obedient when they meet Japanese people. There are many Koreans who practice medicine here, but most of them have few patients. Therefore, so-called practicing medicine is just a facade. They all have side businesses. Because these Koreans are unreasonable, it is difficult for them to rent houses in the market. Landlords fear them like tigers and avoid them for fear of getting close. So they had a strange idea and colluded with Chinese traitors to find out where there were vacant houses for rent, and then they forcibly occupied them without paying rent. Therefore, in recent months, there have been endless rent disputes. The authorities have now decided to punish the Chinese who collude with them to occupy houses with extreme punishment.

Japanese and Korean prostitutes are mostly concentrated in Fanzi Flatboat Alley and other places in the East City. Most of those who frequent these places are Western military police and sailors. Chinese people do not often patronize them. These prostitutes, in addition to sometimes putting on makeup and swaggering through the streets, are not as arrogant as the Japanese and Korean vagrants who rush around everywhere. They are also pitiful insects among the Japanese.

When Sino-Japanese relations were tense, the vagrants caused a lot of trouble. They often visited the residences of relatively well-known Chinese people and asked about their views on Sino-Japanese relations or inquired about their recent whereabouts, which was unbearable. They also often entered and exited various libraries, wearing the badges of the ×× special service organization or the ×× army, regardless of whether they were real or fake. Sometimes they wanted to take away magazines and newspapers, and sometimes they wanted to buy rare books. There were all kinds of unreasonable disturbances.

Apart from the staff of the Japanese Embassy, the other cultural workers and educated Japanese people are very different from the soldiers and vagrants. These Japanese people, in addition to showing a slight arrogance in appearance, are not difficult to get along with. Even the Japanese who run Japanese language tutoring schools and the Japanese students who audit classes at various universities can generally maintain considerable politeness and are easier to get along with than Europeans and Americans with different skin colors and habits. A certain Japanese auditing student at Peking University once questioned a professor for criticizing Japan's violation of international law in an international law class last year, but after the professor explained briefly, the student was convinced and did not argue any further. This is much better than the unreasonableness of the soldiers and vagrants.

National Election Office Notice: Group Staff Members Must Take Supplementary Oath; University Faculty and People from Four Provinces Took Oath Yesterday; Citizen Registration Forms Collected Today

Yesterday was the fifth day for citizens' oath registration in this city. National and registered private universities and independent colleges held their ceremonies at their designated times and locations. People from the four provinces of Liaoning, Jilin, Heilongjiang, and Rehe residing in Shanghai registered and took their oaths at the Youth Propaganda Corps throughout the day. The citizen registration forms for citizens in various districts were distributed door-to-door by a large number of personnel dispatched by the National Election Office yesterday, totaling hundreds of thousands of forms. They are scheduled to be collected today, and the oath-taking methods will be announced separately at a later date. The National Election Office also announced yesterday that professional organizations and freelance professional groups that have not yet registered and taken oaths should complete the procedures within a specified period to ensure no omissions. Details are as follows:

University Separated Oaths

Yesterday, the citizen oath registration for presidents, deans, faculty, staff, and employees of various universities and independent colleges was held in eleven locations. The presidents of the respective schools, including Pei Fuheng (Business School), He Bingsong (Jinan University), Chu Minyi (Sino-French University), Xu Jingxiong (Zhengfeng), Sheng Zhenwei (Soochow University), Cao Huiqun (Datong University), Zhang Shouyong (Guanghua University), etc., presided over the ceremonies. Four Province People Oath

The citizen oath registration for people from Liaoning, Jilin, Heilongjiang, and Rehe residing in this city was held yesterday at the Youth Propaganda Corps. Five to six hundred people attended in accordance with the regulations. Shi Bingyan served as chairman, and Chen Junyi, a member of the city party headquarters, supervised the oath.

City Resident Registration

Yesterday, citizen registration forms for citizens in various districts were first distributed, instructing people to fill them out and return them with the deliverer, or to leave them to be collected by the original distributors today. After these registration forms are collected, oath-taking procedures will be arranged separately at a later date. The time and location will be announced separately. All residents of this city are urged to register enthusiastically in order to obtain citizen certificates and the right to vote in the future. Moreover, citizen registration only needs to be completed once per person. Therefore, those who have already registered and taken oaths in their service units or organizations do not need to fill out the form again to avoid duplication.

Supplementary Oath Notice

The National Election Office yesterday issued Notice No. 10 regarding supplementary oaths for staff members of various professional organizations and freelance professional groups. The notice stated that the city's professional organizations and freelance professional groups had previously held citizen oath registration on a regular basis. However, some staff members of various organizations have not yet participated and should take supplementary oaths to avoid omissions. The following regulations are hereby stipulated for supplementary oath registration: (1) Date: August 20, all day; (2) All directors and councilors of farmers' associations and fishermen's associations, as well as directors and supervisors of guilds who have not registered and taken oaths, will attend the ceremony at the Shanghai General Labor Union, located at Meijialong, Qiaojia Bang, Nanshi; (3) All executive committee members of various trade associations will attend the ceremony at the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce, located at Tianhou Palace Bridge; (4) The accountants' association, journalists' association, medical and pharmaceutical associations, and educational association will attend the ceremony at the Shanghai Public Stadium, Nanshi City Educational Association. For fear of inadequate notification, this announcement is hereby published in the newspaper. Supervisor: Wu Tiecheng.

Seamen's Union Oath

Members of the Chinese Seamen's Union, including firemen, sailors, stewards, cargo handlers, and middle cabin staff, held citizen registration and citizen oath ceremonies at the Chinese Seamen's Union Special Commissioner's Office starting at 9:00 AM yesterday. Yang Xiaotian, the special commissioner of the union, was appointed by the Shanghai Municipal Representative Election Office of the National Assembly to supervise the oath. Secretary Wang Ji presided over the ceremony, and Peng Zhenqiu and Li Jianbai were appointed as clerks. Due to the large number of union members, the ceremonies were held in several sessions. It is reported that a large number of members in Shanghai attended the ceremony.

City Fishermen's Association Requests Explanation

The City Fishermen's Association of this city has many doubts regarding the mixed election of fishermen's and farmers' associations when recommending national election representatives. Therefore, it telegraphed the National Assembly Election Headquarters yesterday to request an explanation. The original telegram is recorded as follows: To Jiang Junjian, Director of the National Assembly Representative Election Headquarters in Nanjing: Upon investigation of Schedule 3 of the National Assembly Representative Election Law, the number of representatives from local farmers' associations and fishermen's associations is four in total, and in principle, there is no distinction. However, the intent of the law is to value both agriculture and fisheries equally, and in coastal areas, fisheries are even more important than agriculture. The hub where fishery products gather and disperse is even more important than agriculture. Under these special circumstances, does the local election office have the authority to consider the advantages and disadvantages and make appropriate divisions to conform to reality? This is the first point requiring explanation. Furthermore, Article 20 of the Election Law stipulates that candidates from each professional organization shall be selected by the executive body of each professional organization. Since each of the farmers' and fishermen's associations is a group with independent status, when recommending candidates, the two associations will inevitably recommend separately, rather than jointly recommend. This seems extremely clear. However, such regulations are inconsistent with the principle stipulated in Schedule 3 of the aforementioned Election Law. When the two associations produce representative candidates, will they be recommended separately, or will they be jointly recommended in name only, while actually designating quotas and setting up separate ballot boxes for separate recommendations? This is a point that requires explanation. The above two points are crucial to electoral policy, and the time is pressing. Please submit them to the Legislative Interpretation Committee for prompt interpretation and telegraph the reply for public convenience. Shanghai Fishermen's Association respectfully.

Wang and Jin, Two Envoys, Depart the Country This Morning; Wang Jingqi Goes to Sweden and Norway to Take Office; Jin Wensi Returns to the Netherlands to Resume His Post

The Remaining Debt of Qian Industry to Three Banks Will Be Cleared Soon

The Dagong News Agency reported that a financial crisis occurred in this city at the end of last year, and the Qian industry was on the verge of danger. With the Ministry of Finance planning to issue 25 million yuan of the Republic of China 24th Year Financial Bonds in June and organizing the Qian Industry Supervision Committee to dismantle and lend to various Qianzhuang, financial stability was achieved. After the Qian industry recovered its vitality, as the loans expired, the Supervision Committee repeatedly urged them to repay them separately. The various Zhuang repaid part of the financial bonds, the 3 million yuan of the Qian Industry Reserve Treasury, and the 4 million yuan of various commercial banks in full before November last year. The remaining 18 million yuan of the Central Bank, Bank of China, and Bank of Communications has also been repaid in installments of 8 or 9 million yuan. The Dismantling and Lending Committee formed by the three banks has repeatedly agreed to accommodate and extend the repayment date for this outstanding balance. According to the Dagong News Agency reporter's investigation of the Qian industry, the financial public debt owed by Henglai and other stores to the three banks has been urged by the Qian Association to find ways to repay it as soon as possible. As a result of business improvements, Henglai and other Zhuang now have thicker capital turnover capabilities and are determined to allocate funds to repay the debt as much as possible. The public debt owed to the three banks before the end of October this year, together with the 8% long-term interest, can be repaid in full.

Important Talk by Vice Minister Chen Jie: Yan Huiqing Resigns and the Successor Has Been Internally Determined; Sino-Russian Friendship and Trade Treaty Still Needs Further Discussion; We Will Add Commissioners to the League of Nations Subcommittees

Chen Jie, Deputy Minister of Foreign Affairs, went to Lushan to attend the Executive Yuan meeting. Ambassador Yan's Resignation Has Been Approved

According to Chen's answer to reporters' questions, Yan Huiqing, our country's ambassador to the Soviet Union, is old and frail and has repeatedly submitted his resignation to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs. There is no way to keep him, and it has been approved. The successor has also been internally determined and has been agreed to by the Soviet Union. It can be officially announced within ten days. Yan has served in the diplomatic community for many years and has made outstanding achievements. After his resignation, he will choose a place in the country to recuperate. Negotiating Sino-Russian Friendship and Trade Treaty

Our Country Will Set Up Commissioners in Various League of Nations Groups

Chen continued to say that the League of Nations has set the end of September to hold a general assembly to discuss the issue of revising the League of Nations rules. The League of Nations has sought opinions from our government. The office established by our country's delegation to the League of Nations in Geneva only has a few staff members stationed when it is not in session. When the meeting is approaching, secretaries from the embassies in Europe are transferred to assist. They are unfamiliar with the place and the staff, so naturally, there are many inconveniences in handling affairs. Therefore, it has been decided to add one or two commissioners from our country to the military, diplomatic, political, and other groups of the League of Nations. They will be stationed in Geneva and can investigate the international situation at any time and represent us at the meetings of various subcommittees.

Minister Zhang also arrived in Lushan on the 15th and is scheduled to return to Beijing at the end of this month. Chen also learned that he could not leave Beijing for a long time due to affairs and will return to Beijing on the night of the 20th.

Chamber of Commerce Telegraphs Ministry of Transportation and Others, Please Open South Seas Route: Near Expensive and Distant Cheap, Foreign Ships Manipulate Arbitrarily, Overcoming All Difficulties Should Take into Account National Economy and People's Livelihood

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce telegraphed the Ministry of Transportation and the Ministry of Industry in Nanjing yesterday: Ministry of Transportation and Ministry of Industry, on the 17th of this month, according to a letter from Nanqiao Bank, since the currency reform in our country, the export of domestic products has increased compared to before. Even flour, a commodity, has not been heard of being transported to the South Seas since the 20th year. Now it is also decided to export it. If so, the expectations for domestic goods to travel abroad are even more likely to take advantage of the opportunity to develop. However, the export of goods depends on the reduction of various expenses and low costs to facilitate sales. Among the various expenses, the freight cost is the most critical. In the past, the freight cost for loading and transporting export goods with Singapore or Penang as the destination was 10 yuan per ton of national currency, discounted by 90% or 80%. Recently, it has been unreasonably increased to 14 or 15 yuan per ton of national currency, which makes the cost suddenly increase and the export of domestic products is greatly hindered. It is found that the freight cost charged by various shipping companies for goods transported from Shanghai to Columbus is only 9 yuan per ton of national currency. It is also found that the freight cost for goods transported from Dalian to Singapore or Penang is only 8 yuan. In terms of water distance, Shanghai is closer to Singapore and Penang than Columbus. Even from Dalian to Singapore or Penang, the water distance is farther than from Shanghai. There is no reason for the near to be expensive and the far to be cheap. This kind of non-standard and unfair regulation clearly shows that their intention is to invisibly restrict the export of our country's products. The reason for this is that our country does not have ships sailing abroad, and all export goods rely solely on foreign ships for transportation, allowing them to manipulate the market. If we do not take urgent measures to rescue the situation, the future of domestic products will have no chance to be sold abroad. The council is the hub of merchants and the guide for the promotion of domestic products. Seeing this situation, it should also feel the urgency and seek ways to remedy it. Therefore, we earnestly request your council to negotiate with various shipping companies based on the current method of governance, reduce the freight charges, and make accurate regulations to avoid the near being more expensive than the far, so as to facilitate the export of domestic products. Furthermore, we request the state-run China Merchants Bureau to open the South Seas route in the shortest possible time to recover the benefits and facilitate transportation, so that the future of domestic products will have a chance to be sold abroad. After investigating, the two strategies of short-term and long-term treatment presented by the bank, from a fair point of view, the short-term treatment method is in the hands of the people. In the past, foreign ships sailing in the country increased freight charges, and there was still an opportunity to negotiate and reduce them. The reason is that there are already domestic ships participating in the route, and foreign ships cannot manipulate the market alone. Therefore, negotiations are still easy to comply with. The recent change in the calculation standard of the transport price on the Yangtze River route is an example. As for foreign routes, which are exclusively dominated by foreign ships, there is no place to restrain them slightly, so it is not easy to achieve the effect of negotiation and transformation. Moreover, from the perspective of foreign merchants' national policies, since the implementation of the legal currency policy, the export prices of goods have been reduced, and countries that have a vested interest in us are secretly jealous of us. Their plan to increase freight charges is a hidden attempt to obstruct us, and the situation is even more obvious. Rather than begging them for mercy, which is only met with contempt, it is better to overcome all difficulties and seek solutions within ourselves. Moreover, opening the South Seas route has been a consistent request of overseas Chinese for years. The China Merchants Bureau is state-run, and if the government's strength is slightly supported, even if the initial operation is not without deficits, the overall medical plan will still benefit the national economy and people's livelihood. Otherwise, year after year, the Yellow River will be difficult to wait for. Not only will the overseas Chinese be discouraged, but the international transportation network will be controlled by others for a long time, and foreign trade will have no hope of prosperity. This matter should be planned with all the power of the government. If the China Merchants Bureau is ordered to recognize the restoration, it will inevitably repeat the mistakes of the Singapore Chinese Chamber of Commerce's request in the previous session, delaying the years and making it difficult to achieve success. Therefore, the sincerity of Shanghai sincerely appeals to the capital to take charge of planning and implementation, so that it can be realized, which is for public convenience. Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce respectfully.

Bureau of Unified Taxation Investigates and Detains People and Goods; Liang Shao Alcohol Business Suspends Operations Yesterday

Representatives Dispatched to Petition the Authorities, Who Agreed to Release Detainees; Bail Procedures Completed, Resumption of Operations Expected Today

The Shanghai Liang Shao Alcohol Industry Guild reports that Unified Taxation Bureau investigators from the Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Anhui region, alleging that the industry was substituting alcohol for shao alcohol, detained and punished individuals and goods. As a result, wholesale transactions were suspended starting yesterday, while retail operations continued as usual. Representatives were dispatched to petition the authorities. The details are as follows:

Suspension of Wholesale Operations: A total of forty-two Liang Shao alcohol businesses, including Tongxinchang, Tongchangfu, Wanyuanshun, Laohengxing, and Tongheyong, convened a meeting of guild members due to the Unified Taxation Bureau investigators from the Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Anhui, and Jiangxi region detaining and punishing people and goods, alleging that they were substituting alcohol for shao alcohol. A decision was made to temporarily suspend operations. As of yesterday, all businesses ceased wholesale transactions and stopped deliveries, as any goods found by Unified Taxation Bureau investigators would be detained. Even orders already placed by customers awaiting delivery were reluctantly suspended. However, retail operations continued as usual. Regarding the individuals and goods detained by the Unified Taxation Bureau of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Anhui, and Jiangxi, apart from Lai Afang and Zai Ancai of Tongchangfu Alcohol Business, and Shi Agou of Tongheyong Alcohol Business, along with their boats and goods, the rest were bailed out from the Unified Taxation Bureau by their respective businesses.

Emergency Meeting: The Liang Shao Alcohol Industry Guild held an emergency meeting of its members yesterday at 2:00 PM at its meeting place located at No. 265 Maojia Lane in the Nanshi district. Representatives from forty-two businesses, including Tongxinchang, Tongheyong, and Wanyuangong, attended. He Xiangsheng, the chairman, reported on the incident in which Unified Taxation Bureau investigators from the Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Anhui region detained and punished members' delivered goods, alleging the substitution of alcohol for shao alcohol. Following this, discussions commenced regarding dispatching representatives to petition the authorities. It was decided on the spot to appoint He Xiangsheng, Jin Depei, Huang Huade, Xu Shilong, Wang Wenbin, and Li Guoqing as representatives to petition the Unified Taxation Bureau of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Anhui, requesting sanctions against the investigators who were forcibly accusing them of substituting alcohol, the release of the detained delivery personnel and goods from the alcohol businesses, and guarantees that similar incidents would not occur in the future. The meeting adjourned around 3:00 PM.

Petition to Stop Abuses: At 3:30 PM yesterday, the Liang Shao Alcohol Industry Guild dispatched representatives He Xiangsheng, Jin Depei, Huang Huade, Xu Shilong, Wang Wenbin, and Ji Guoqing to the Unified Taxation Bureau of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Anhui on Dagu Road to petition. Department head Jiang Jinkai received them. He Xiangsheng first recounted the details of the alcohol businesses' goods being detained for allegedly substituting alcohol. Department head Jiang, in addition to urging the resumption of wholesale transactions, promised to immediately instruct the Investigation Division to promptly report the details of the penalties for alcohol substitution for verification. He also agreed to release the detained personnel and instructed them to submit a formal written petition. The representatives left around 4:00 PM.

Tax Bureau Statement: A reporter from the Xin Sheng News Agency spoke with Department head Jin of the Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Anhui Unified Taxation Bureau yesterday. He stated that the Ministry of Finance has repeatedly issued orders prohibiting alcohol substitution and has stipulated penalty measures. Therefore, investigators will detain and punish those found to be substituting alcohol. If there is any doubt about the detained goods, they will be sent to the Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau of the Ministry of Industry for inspection. The bureau has not yet received reports from its subordinate districts regarding the alcohol substitution goods detained by investigators this time. It has now instructed them to report promptly for verification. As for the suspension of wholesale transactions by the Liang Shao alcohol industry, they have been urged to resume operations, he said.

Release and Resumption of Operations: A reporter from the Xin Zheng News Agency met with He Xiangsheng, chairman of the Liang Shao Alcohol Industry Guild, last night. According to him, the Unified Taxation Bureau required the filling out of a penalty acknowledgment form when bailing out the delivery personnel of the detained alcohol businesses. Therefore, after bailing them out, it was considered an admission of alcohol substitution. It was resolved to suspend wholesale transactions. As a result of the petition, the Unified Taxation Bureau has agreed to release the detained personnel, goods, and boats on bail and waive the penalty acknowledgment form. The industry has decided to resume transactions as soon as the personnel and goods are released. Furthermore, it was originally planned to cease the loading of shao alcohol boats heading to Shanghai from Jiangbei and anchoring at the Xinqiao docks, starting on the 19th. If the bail procedures are completed today, this measure can be avoided.

The Daishan Tragedy

The Zhejiang Provincial Government Responds to Telegrams from Two Fellow-Provincial Associations; Zhang Zhongli Discusses the Handling of the Case

Due to the forced collection of salt taxes by the fishery and salt tax police in Daishan, Zhejiang Province, a tragic incident occurred. The Ningbo and Dinghai Fellow-Provincial Associations in Shanghai, as well as Yu Qiaqing, Liu Hongsheng, and others, telegraphed the Zhejiang Provincial Government requesting proper handling of the matter. A reply telegram was received yesterday, stating: To Mr. Yu Qiaqing of the Ningbo Fellow-Provincial Association in Shanghai and Mr. Liu Hongsheng of the Dinghai Fellow-Provincial Association in Shanghai: Your telegrams of the "Zhen" and "Zheng" series have been received. Upon investigation, the Zhejiang Provincial Executive Committee, the Zhejiang Public Assembly, the Ningbo Fellow-Provincial Association in Beijing, and Zhuang Songfu, a citizen of Fenghua, have all submitted letters and telegrams to the government. The matter has been referred to the Ministry of Finance and the Liangzhe Salt Transport Commissioner for review and response, and Commissioner Zhao has been ordered to supervise the Daishan County Magistrate in handling the aftermath properly. In addition to forwarding the "Zheng" telegram to the Salt Transport Commissioner for filing and review, we are sending this telegraph in advance. Chairman of the Zhejiang Provincial Government, with two official seals.

Zhang Zhongli, Director of the Liangzhe Salt Affairs Tax Police Bureau, came to Shanghai yesterday on official business. A reporter from the Central News Agency visited him to inquire about the cause of the riot and the details of the incident. Zhang's response was as follows:

Centralized Salt Storage is Beneficial and Harmless

Centralized salt storage is the initial step in implementing the new salt law and is intended to benefit both fishermen and salt producers. Within the Liangzhe region, areas such as Nan Salt, Changlin, Qingquan, and Dinghai have already implemented this system. In the past, salt producers in Daishan transported and sold their salt themselves without warehousing, making management difficult and hindering the implementation of on-site tax collection. For salt producers, price drops were common during periods of slow sales. Conversely, when production was insufficient, fishermen often faced high salt prices. The centralized storage system is divided into facilities for both fishery salt and table salt. Fishery salt storage facilities are built in areas where fishing boats congregate, with wharves constructed for tax payment and salt distribution, ensuring timeliness and efficiency. In the event of production shortages, the government plans to provide loans for distribution. On-site tax collection eliminates inspection procedures and other inconveniences. For table salt, the government is responsible for storage, eliminating the risk of loss. The construction of roads within the storage areas facilitates transportation, and salt prices are standardized to prevent competition. In the event of slow sales, the government provides loans for adjustment. The methods for collecting and distributing salt and the timing of these activities are all coordinated appropriately. Claims that salt producers cannot deliver salt to the storage facilities or fishermen cannot purchase salt outside of salt office hours are deliberately provocative and untrue. Therefore, centralized salt storage is the only way to achieve scientific management and is the initial step in implementing the new salt law. It benefits the legitimate business of salt producers and fishermen and is only detrimental to private buying and selling. There is no reason to oppose it.

Fishery Salt Coloring Prevents Illegal Sales

Fishery salt coloring is intended to prevent the illegal sale of table salt. Ministry orders have been issued for some time, and all regions are implementing this measure. Daishan is not the first. As the second-largest salt-producing area in Liangzhe and a major fishing region nationwide, Daishan is no exception. Furthermore, the coloring agent has been carefully considered and tested by experts from both the Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Industry before implementation. It will not cause mold or spoilage. The reason for the widespread opposition is that once the salt is colored, it becomes difficult to sell illegally. In other words, it is no longer possible to sell fishery salt taxed at three cents as table salt taxed at seven yuan and ten cents. Investigations have revealed that Daishan alone illegally sells approximately 400,000 dan of fishery salt taxed at three cents as table salt taxed at seven yuan and ten cents in the five prefectures of Suzhou each year, causing a loss of three million yuan in national tax revenue. The state encourages the fishing industry by providing lower taxes, but this is being exploited for private gain. The government's implementation of fishery salt coloring as a preventive measure is entirely justified. Moreover, the Wenzhou and Taizhou prefectures have been implementing this measure since last year without any obstacles. Its implementation in the Dinghai and Daishan regions this year will not harm the legitimate interests of fishermen, it can be stated with certainty.

The Course of the Fishery and Salt Riot

The Daishan fishery and salt riot on July 13 was organized in advance. Individuals who have traditionally exploited the fishery and salt industry first convened a meeting at the Zifusi Salt Industry Credit Cooperative on July 10, using inflammatory language to oppose centralized storage. On July 11, they collectively stopped salt production. On July 12, a salt producer named Huang Bao-ren continued to produce salt, resulting in the destruction of his salt slabs. Li Ren-fu, who attempted to reason with them, was dragged to the Dongyue Temple and beaten. Village head Huang Gong reported the incident, and the Public Security Bureau rescued him from danger. On July 13, they convened another large meeting of fishermen and salt producers at the Dongyue Temple. As the crowd grew larger, violence erupted. First, they captured Liu Feng-sheng, a surveyor from the engineering office, and severely beat him. His wife, upon hearing this, rushed to the weighing and distribution station to seek help. A team led by Captain Hu, along with several police officers from the Public Security Bureau, went to rescue him. On the way, they encountered the crowd, who were bringing the surveyor bound. Captain Hu, fearing misunderstandings, ordered the police to stop and only took Sergeant Xu Li forward to reason with them. The crowd swarmed forward and seized Xu Li's wooden-cased gun. While they were struggling, rioters opened fire, knocking Xu Li down. The violence escalated from there. In this incident, several thousand rioters killed nine salt affairs personnel and seriously injured three others. Many were disemboweled, had their hearts removed, and were thrown into the sea. The cruelty was horrifying. During the rioters' siege of the bureau team, they fired frequently. The walls are still riddled with bullet holes. Even those who understand the situation say that they were unarmed. At the time, Captain Hu responded cautiously and strictly prohibited the police from firing live rounds. Therefore, only one fisherman and salt producer died during the major riot.

Handling the Aftermath with Leniency and Harmony

Since the riot, the salt affairs authorities have consistently advocated for leniency and harmony. I arrived in Ningbo on July 19 and met with Commissioner Zhao to discuss the handling of the aftermath. He expressed sympathy for my views. He agreed that the ringleaders should be severely punished, but that those who were coerced should not be implicated. Together with Magistrate Shen of Dinghai, we developed several measures to stabilize the situation and notified the public. Daishan's market resumed on July 15, and salt producers resumed salt production on July 18. By July 22, everything was back to normal. There was no mass exodus or starvation. Some fishermen and salt producers who participated in the killings and arson are afraid to return, but the salt affairs authorities cannot be held responsible for this. As for adjusting the police force, the order was issued beforehand and was unavoidable. After the incident on July 13, we telegraphed the headquarters, requesting that the Jian'an patrol ship and two companies from Cui's battalion of the Tax Police Regiment come to Daishan for reinforcement. Because the ship transportation took time, we transferred the Guerrilla Brigade stationed in Ningbo to Daishan as a temporary measure on July 17. On July 21, at the request of Commissioner Zhao, we withdrew the Guerrilla Brigade back to its original defense area, leaving only one company stationed in Daqu and Liangshan. Later, due to rumors among the fishermen and salt producers in Daishan about a second riot, we received an order from the sub-bureau to transfer the withdrawn two companies back to Daishan. In early August, the two companies of Cui's battalion arrived in Zhejiang, so we dispatched one company to be stationed in Daqu and Liangshan, and transferred the entire Guerrilla Brigade back to Ningbo. The current number of troops in Daishan is two-thirds less than before. The outside world's belief that we increased the number of troops is a misunderstanding. Regarding the arrest of criminals, apart from the arrest of Abbot Xinliang, who was involved in instigating the riot, which I discussed with Magistrate Shen, no one else has been arrested in Daishan. However, more than twenty fugitives were arrested in Xiangshan Port due to the discovery of stolen goods, weapons, and evidence of the riot during the investigation of illegal salt sales. All were handed over to the judicial authorities for impartial handling, which is different from indiscriminate arrest and implication.

The Current Key Objectives: Reorganizing Salt Administration

In summary, the matters concerning centralized salt storage and fishery salt coloring were originally ordered by the Ministry of Finance and are part of the salt administration, not the responsibility of the tax police. However, due to unforeseen changes, responsibilities are intertwined. Recently, I have read in the newspapers that criticism has been directed at the tax police. I do not wish to argue further. Fortunately, the tax police in Liangzhe are diligent in their duties, and tax revenue has now increased to more than two million. Local bandits have been suppressed in four provinces. The facts are clear. Some believe that we must sympathize with the suffering of the fishermen and salt producers, which is certainly a compassionate sentiment. However, the suffering stems from the fact that everything is not yet on the right track. Now, as we implement the salt law and reorganize salt administration, continuing to protect temporary and improper interests and disregarding national laws is not a fundamental solution. Furthermore, with the national crisis and dwindling financial resources, customs duties are currently affected by smuggling, and salt taxes in Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Huai, and Fujian are the only reliable sources. According to population and tax rates, Liangzhe should collect 15 million yuan in salt tax each year, but in recent years, the revenue has not reached ten million, due to the loss of hundreds of thousands of yuan from fishery salt sales in the five prefectures of Suzhou. The total loss to the national treasury is significant, while the improper interests of the fishermen and salt producers are limited. There must be other ways in which they are being exploited. The national treasury suffers significant losses, but the poverty of the fishermen and salt producers remains unchanged. The reason for this deserves deep thought. If centralized salt storage and fishery salt coloring can be fully implemented, not only will the salt tax be thoroughly reorganized, but the fishermen and salt producers will also benefit greatly. It is beneficial for both the national economy and the people's livelihood.

Sun Kaigen Returns to Shanghai from Gansu, Discusses the Progress of the Tao Hui Canal Project

Shanghai News Agency reports that the National Economic Commission, in order to revitalize water conservancy in Gansu Province, allocated 500,000 yuan for water conservancy projects in the province in the summer of 1934, to be constructed in phases. The Lintao Hui Canal was included in the first phase of water conservancy projects, with an allocation of 55,000 yuan. A canal design and survey team was dispatched to Gansu to work on the project. Sun Kaigen, a member of the team, returned to Shanghai yesterday. A reporter from the Shanghai News Agency interviewed Sun Kaigen to discuss the progress of the project. His account is as follows:

Project Overview

According to Sun, the canal's water intake is located near the Da Hu Li family in the southern countryside of Lin County, diverting water from the Tao River, a tributary of the Yellow River. The main canal is 28 kilometers long, running from Baita in the south to Shengouyan in the north, irrigating approximately 36,000 mu of land in the north and south areas of Lintao. The canal line mostly runs along hillsides and foothills, requiring numerous flood discharge tunnels. The valleys and gullies crossed by the canal are all mountain watercourses, with widths reaching over 140 meters and depths reaching 15-16 meters. During the dry season, the flow in the gullies is minimal, sometimes even drying up completely. However, during sudden heavy rains in the summer, the flood flow can reach 600-700 cubic meters per second. The soil in the irrigation area consists of a loess layer at the top, a gravel layer in the middle, and a red soil layer at the bottom. For construction projects, stone is used below the flood level, and wood is used above the flood level, as local stone is scarce and expensive, while wood is abundant and inexpensive. The canal project includes a main canal, water intake, intake gate, spillway dam, reduction gate, tunnels, dredging channels, culverts, bridges, weirs, and branch gates.

Progress Overview

I was ordered to go to Gansu in September last year to assist in the supervision of the Tao Hui Canal project. I arrived at the Lintao construction site in October and immediately began to replace missing stakes, prepare for excavation, supervise the transportation of materials, and attempt to attract merchants to contract various construction projects. However, due to the tense situation of the bandit suppression campaign at that time, the requisition of laborers for repairing the airfield, building bunkers, and repairing the automobile road was affected to some extent. As of now, the first phase of earthwork has been completed. According to the first section of the main canal, due to the terrain, the canal body has been excavated to a depth of more than 10 meters, and the stone canal section at the canal mouth is expected to be quite labor-intensive. As for construction projects, materials are currently being transported, and contracts for the gully, Dongyu gully, and Yang gully aqueducts are being negotiated with outside contractors. It is currently planned that small projects will be constructed by local craftsmen, while larger projects will be contracted by outside contractors.

All Sectors Donate Funds to Purchase Aircraft for Birthday Celebration

The China Aviation Association Expands the National Aviation Salvation Movement; Shanghai Municipality Collects Funds to Purchase Aircraft to Present to the Government as a Birthday Commemoration for Chairman Chiang Kai-shek. Taikoo Company's New Ning Shipwrecked

Hurricane Strikes, Passengers and Crew Safe

The Taikoo Company's New Ning sustained the most damage of all commercial vessels struck by the hurricane in Hong Kong. The ship was departing from Guangdong with cargo and passengers for Hong Kong. It encountered the hurricane near Mount Ni-Te and attempted to reach Shachuan Bay for shelter, but it was too late. It dropped both anchors off Mount Ni-Te, but the wind was too strong, and the waves were too high. The ship was driven by the wind, and both anchors broke. The hull of the New Ning was struck by the hurricane and crashed into the foot of Mount Ni-Te, causing the hull to be breached by the rocks. Seawater flooded in. It did not strike a reef. Fortunately, the Hong Kong marine and land police dispatched barges at great risk to rescue all the passengers who had boarded the ship in Guangdong. The wind gradually shifted toward Guangxi Province around 5:00 PM on the 17th. Therefore, all the passengers were rescued. The crew was also safe. Taikoo Company's Hong Kong branch is assisting in the rescue efforts. However, the hull of the New Ning has been shattered and may sink at the location. It is uncertain whether the cargo can be salvaged. Efforts are underway to salvage the mail and other items. This ship was an excellent vessel in Taikoo's South China fleet, with a deadweight of 2,550 tons. Its hull was excellent, and it was a regular liner on the Shanghai-Shantou-Hong Kong route. The company will dispatch another ship to replace it.

The British Company's British India Mail ship Talma was also struck by the storm and drifted 12 nautical miles. Fortunately, it drifted into a harbor and did not sustain major damage. The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Haizhen was fortunate. Yesterday, the company received a telegram from Guangdong stating that the Haizhen was safe and unharmed.

Industrial Accident Statistics for July

Eleven Deaths and Ninety-two Injuries; Published by the Factory Inspection Division of the Social Affairs Bureau

The Factory Inspection Division of the Shanghai Municipal Social Affairs Bureau has released industrial accident statistics for July, totaling 103 incidents: nine male workers and two female workers died, and seventy-eight male workers and fourteen female workers were injured. The causes of the accidents are listed below: (1) Power-driven machinery: one female worker died, thirteen male workers and eleven female workers were injured; (2) Electrocution: three male workers died, one male worker was injured; (3) Explosion: four male workers died; (4) Fire: one male worker was injured; (5) High-temperature objects and corrosive substances: ten male workers were injured; (6) Falls: three male workers and one female worker died, seven male workers and one female worker were injured; (7) Handling of objects: twenty-two male workers were injured; (8) Falling objects: two male workers were injured; (9) Stepping on or colliding with objects: three male workers and one female worker were injured; (10) Unknown causes: three male workers were injured; (11) Other causes: one male worker died, six male workers and one female worker were injured. The total number of accidents increased by 18 compared to June.

Family Property Dispute Entangles Coffins Stored at Cemetery

Siming Public Cemetery Groundlessly Accused

Shen Dong, the wife of the owner of Shen He-tai Fruit Shop at No. 296-298 Fada Road, is 76 years old and has three sons. The shop is managed jointly by the three sons. However, the eldest son, Shen Jin-you, and the second son, Shen Jin-cai, are illiterate and only handle external sales. The third son, Jin-fu, attended school and is responsible for the shop's accounts and finances. Unfortunately, Jin-fu fell ill and passed away in July of last year, leaving behind a young widow, Lin, and a biological daughter, Yin-zhu. The Shen family started in the fruit business in Shanghai and accumulated considerable wealth, which has not yet been divided. Jin-fu's widow, Shen Lin, unable to bear the bullying and abuse of her mother-in-law and sisters-in-law, took her daughter, Yin-zhu, and returned to her mother's home in Ningbo on May 1 of this year, seeking a new life. After Lin and her daughter left, Shen Dong and her sons Jin-you and Jin-cai hired a lawyer and filed a lawsuit in the Second Special District Court, accusing Shen Lin of seizing their property. Shen Lin, acting as the legal guardian of her daughter, Yin-zhu, also hired lawyer Xu Wu-fang and filed a lawsuit in the Second Special District Court against her mother-in-law and brothers-in-law, seeking a division of the property. The parties have been suing each other, and the cases have not yet concluded. Recently, Shen Lin learned that her mother-in-law had reported the loss of the coffin storage ticket at Siming Public Cemetery, where her husband's coffin was stored, and prevented her from retrieving it. Shen Lin approached the cemetery to no avail and filed a lawsuit in the Second Special District Court against the manager of Siming Public Cemetery, seeking the return of the coffin containing the remains of Shen Jin-fu, coffin number 15766, which had been entrusted to the cemetery. The court accepted the case and held a hearing yesterday morning at 8:00 AM, presided over by Judge Wu Xiao-ke, summoning both parties for mediation. The plaintiff requested the court to order the return of the coffin. The defendant stated that because of the plaintiff's family dispute, the coffin storage ticket had been reported lost, and the cemetery could not release the coffin to either party. It was necessary to wait for the court to rule on which party was entitled to retrieve the coffin. The cemetery was not obstructing the process. After verifying the statements, the court declared the mediation unsuccessful and adjourned.

National Products Promotion at Sports Meet; Promoting Domestically Produced Beverages and Food

Letter to the Chamber of Commerce Requesting a Meeting with the Restaurant and Wine Industries to Discuss the Issue of Displaying Certification Plaques

We plan to issue certification plaques to establishments that stock domestically produced beverages and food, which will be displayed in the establishments and promoted to the public. We have completed the inspection and research of implementation measures. We would like to request that your chamber invite the responsible persons of the restaurant industry guild to meet with Mr. Wang Xing-yao, the director of our association's domestic products promotion department, to discuss the next steps. The meeting should be held in your chamber's conference room for convenience. We would be grateful if you could assist us with this request and inform us of the scheduled date and time in advance."

Restaurant Industry Consults: Opinions on Extra Tips

The Shanghai Restaurant Industry Association is soliciting opinions from its members regarding the New Life Movement's ban on extra tips. A notice was issued yesterday, stating: "To the esteemed members, regarding the New Life Movement's ban on extra tips, we have received a notice from the Municipal Chamber of Commerce. This association has sent representatives to attend discussions with relevant industry members and police authorities to discuss implementation measures. The first meeting was attended by Standing Committee Member Cheng Kefan at the Municipal Party Headquarters' New Life Movement meeting, requesting the New Life Movement to collect well-implemented measures from other provinces and cities for deliberation. On August 14th, Standing Committee Member Li Mancun from the Cantonese group and Standing Committee Member Hu Yuantang from the Anhui group attended the discussion, and the New Life Movement revised the draft measures. The principles in Article 3 of the implementation measures announced by the New Life Movement Headquarters seem to have discrepancies. On August 16th, the Standing Committee discussed and expressed support for banning extra tips. After examining Articles 4 and 5 of the implementation measures announced by the New Life Movement Headquarters, there seem to be doubts. Extortion should be sanctioned, but the point of whether lawful gratuities should be penalized needs to be studied. Furthermore, there is no consistency in the salaries of different industry groups, and the selection of personnel is determined by both labor and management. Extortion of extra tips from customers should be banned, and the fault lies with the individual, without implicating the member businesses. We have hypothetically made several points, as follows: (1) Upon implementation of the ban on extra tips, customers' voluntary and lawful gratuities should not be restricted. (2) If a waiter or employee is found to have extorted extra tips from customers, they will be penalized, without implicating the establishment. (3) The handling of gratuities should be determined by each business based on their existing good practices. Regarding the salaries of employees and workers, employers and employees should agree on their own. Extra demands from customers are absolutely prohibited, otherwise, they are solely responsible. (4) Regarding the implementation steps for the New Life Movement Promotion Headquarters' announced measures to ban extra tips, each industry must formulate its own detailed rules, as each industry has its own customs and different situations. However, our member businesses do not have the custom of security deposits, and should not be compared with other industries. Regarding the above four points, please participate with your opinions and submit further suggestions from the industry, combine them, handle them, and announce the implementation. Attached is a copy of the New Life Movement Headquarters' announced measures. Please submit them in writing within three days to the association for review."

Eastern Yuhang Road: Counterfeit Currency Operation Busted, Printing Equipment Seized, Three Arrested and Prosecuted

Huishan Patrol Room's Chinese Detective Zhou Guisen, Detectives Sun Aizhong, Li Peijin, Shen Binkui, and Wu Dekui, at 2:30 PM the day before yesterday, busted a counterfeit Central Bank ten-yuan legal tender operation at 932 Heng'er Lane, Eastern Yuhang Road. Three suspects were arrested: Zhang Ruigen (the second landlord of the house), Cai Lianghuai, and He Chunjuan from Shaoxing. They confiscated two machines, eight copper plates, five plaster plates, five ink rollers, twenty-two picture plates, five steel-nib pens, four cans of ink, one bottle each of oil essence and hydrochloric acid, four cups of color, one sheet of multi-layered paper, several pounds of red powder, rosin powder, talcum powder, and white powder, seven packages of counterfeit currency white paper, one genuine Central Bank ten-yuan note numbered SX400503II, and one printed counterfeit note, along with fourteen unprinted notes. They were taken to the patrol room. Yesterday morning, they were escorted to the Criminal Court No. 3 of the First Special District Court. Attorney Zhang Shizhu of the Public Works Department filed a public prosecution in accordance with Article 195 of the Criminal Law regarding counterfeiting currency, stating that the principal offender, Zhang A'da, was still at large and requested an extension. According to the report from the Chinese and Western detectives, the case was solved after a tip-off to the patrol room from an informant, according to Lin Shiliang, the representative of the Central Bank. Upon questioning, Tong Ruigen confessed that Zhang A'da had rented the rear building from him for two weeks, denying being a shareholder in the operation. The others gave evasive answers. Cai Lianghuai confessed that on the 31st of last month, he was invited by his friend Zhang A'da to print the counterfeit notes, and was initially paid 20 yuan. Later, because the printing was not good, he invited He Chunjuan to print a genuine Central Bank ten-yuan note, which Zhang A'da brought as a sample to copy. After printing, it was handed over to Zhang Ruigen for safekeeping. He Chunjuan confessed that on the 2nd of this month, Cai Lianghuai introduced him to the operation, and he started working there on the 4th. He was only initially paid 5 yuan. Zhang A'da came every day to inspect the work and was out when the arrest was made. The others gave evasive answers. Judge Xiao Xieffen ordered them to be remanded in custody.

In the pauper's asylum at the intersection of Liuying Road and Song Park Road, Zhabei, Shao Xin'da, who is over 60 years old and from Kunshan, stayed at the asylum because he had no relatives. Fish Market: Buying and Selling Salted Goods

Two Fish Firms Request Concessions: Board of Directors to Discuss

Since the Shanghai Fish Market of the Ministry of Industry began selling salted and dried fish goods on August 1st, business has been good. However, the Yan Kang and Gong Shun fish firms, which specialize in salted fish transactions, have not yet moved into the market. Previously, Director Tang Chengzong and others were sent to persuade them, and they have gradually become more amenable. However, the two fish firms have requested to join as brokers and also suggest that the business method be changed, with salted fish sales taking place at the original location in the Sixteenth Settlement, and the fish market sending someone to copy the accounts and collect commissions. The reason given is that the fish market is relatively small, and there is no fixed time for salted fish transactions, as they occur throughout the day, so it is more convenient at the original location. It is reported that the fish market will hold a board of directors meeting within days to discuss this matter. It seems that the request to add one seat for brokers may be accepted, but the request to change the business method will not be considered because it violates the business regulations.

China Merchants Steam Navigation Company Announces: Successful Bidders for Central Wharf Lighterage

China Merchants Steam Navigation Company solicited bids for the lighterage of the Central Wharf. The bidding was opened on the 15th of this month. It is reported that the company reviewed the bids and, in addition to the principle of the lowest bid price, also paid close attention to the bidders' experience. Therefore, the result of the review was that the bid price for the first bid was 73%, and the bid price for the second bid was 74%. The difference between the two bids was only 1%, but because the bidder for the second bid, Zhang Xiaobao, had experience in contracting for lighterage and had more experience, Zhang Xiaobao was selected as the successful bidder, and Huang Bingming was the alternate successful bidder. The other bids were deemed to have excessively high bid prices and were not qualified. It is also reported that this Thursday (i.e., the 20th) is the bidding date for the South Wharf (i.e., Jin Liyuan). It is understood that the South Wharf is the company's own wharf. According to the person in charge of the company, the payment of the lighterage fee for the wharf will be prioritized when the company receives the customer's payment, to assist the contractor in turnover and achieve the purpose of mutual assistance.

Provincial Telegram Price Reduction

The Telegraph Bureau Received an Order from the Ministry: To Be Implemented on the First of Next Month

In order to develop transportation and reduce the burden on the people, the Ministry of Communications has specially reduced the provincial thunder fee and intra-city report fee. The Shanghai Telegraph Bureau has recently received a formal order from the Ministry of Communications, which will be implemented on the first of next month. The Huadong News Agency reporter specially investigated and recorded the following yesterday morning:

Clear and Secret Telegraph Codes: 30% Discount

The Ministry of Communications' domestic telegraph prices, business telegraphs, Chinese clear code 10 cents, secret code 20 cents, foreign clear code 20 cents, secret code 40 cents, regardless of provincial boundaries. Now, in order to develop transportation, the provincial telegraph fee will be charged at a 30% discount on the original price, clear code Chinese 7 cents, secret code 14 cents, and so on.

Name and Address: Charging Method

The original name and address of the recipient, if it is within 15 characters, is charged according to 5 characters. Now it has been changed to calculate one character for every two characters, but it is only limited to this province.

Intra-City Telegrams: 50% Discount

As for intra-city telegrams (that is, sending from this city to this city), the original price was 5 cents per character, but now it has been reduced to 2.5 cents per character. In addition, the original price of Muben Province news telegrams was 2.5 cents per character, but now it has been reduced to 2 cents, all of which are scheduled to be implemented at the same time.

Numerous Idle Vehicles: Rickshaw Industry in Decline

Since the establishment of the Municipal Council Vehicle Committee, the rickshaw industry in this city has been repeatedly suppressed, and business has plummeted. After the Vehicle Committee restricted the number of rickshaw pullers who could register, there are now more rickshaws than pullers. On the one hand, unregistered pullers have no rickshaws to pull; on the other hand, registered pullers have left Shanghai or returned to their hometowns to farm, resulting in many idle rickshaws. The situation has become more serious since the beginning of summer. Currently, the average number of rickshaws operating each day is less than half. Even the mutual aid fee, which should be paid by the pullers, has become an additional burden due to idle rickshaws. Rickshaw owners are losing a significant amount of money every day. Most smaller operations are unable to sustain themselves. Every time taxes are due, they borrow from all sides and pawn everything they own. If this continues, the future of the rickshaw industry is unimaginable. At the same time, the Vehicle Committee has recently been rigorously inspecting and punishing rickshaws. Rickshaws are often ordered to suspend operations for a month or half a month, and rickshaw owners can only bear the pain and accept it. It is also reported that recently, more than a thousand unregistered unemployed pullers have been arrested and fined by the police in the past half-month. These pullers are experiencing extreme hardship due to unemployment. Once arrested and fined, their cries of sorrow are truly heartbreaking. In this city, 300,000 people depend on rickshaws for their livelihood. This situation has serious implications for the future of society.

Xu Ada, a Shaoxing native residing at No. 7, Lane 349, Jiangyin Street, Xiaoximen, was destitute. He borrowed five yuan at usurious interest to buy ginkgo nuts to sell hot ginkgo, hoping to earn a meager profit to support his wife and children. On the afternoon of the 16th of this month, at 8:00 PM, he went out with his burden. A local thug named Xiao Sanzi demanded protection money from him. Xu pleaded bitterly, saying that the capital was borrowed at usurious interest, and begged for exemption. Xiao Sanzi then snatched Xu Ada's ginkgo bag. Xu's eleven-year-old son, Ji Fa, who was nearby, saw someone bullying his father and stepped forward to grab it back. Xiao Sanzi pushed him forcefully, causing him to fall to the ground and suffer serious injuries. Xu immediately ordered his wife, Xu Chen, to take him home. His son's face was pale, and his breath was faint. They rushed him to the New General Charity Hall, but the treatment was ineffective. He died at 3:00 PM the next afternoon. They immediately reported the incident to the police station in charge, and Xiao Sanzi was arrested and sent to the Public Security Bureau for investigation. Yesterday, they ordered the local security officer, Police Officer Yang, to report to the local court for investigation.
