Shanghai Local Supplement of Shen Bao

Talks

A Further Step in Mass Tuberculosis Screening

— Wen

The Hongqiao Sanatorium in this city, with the assistance of the Municipal Health Bureau and the Tuberculosis Prevention Association, will hold a mass X-ray tuberculosis screening starting on the 11th of this month. To check whether you have tuberculosis, you only need to spend one dollar to purchase a ticket and go for the examination. The price of retrieving the examination photo is also particularly low. An X-ray examination in an ordinary hospital costs no less than ten dollars, and the highest price is several tens of dollars. This mass examination only costs one dollar, which is extremely low. This is truly a blessing for the citizens.

However, we still have one opinion. If the examination proves that there is indeed tuberculosis, what should be done for further treatment? This is not a problem for those with ample means. They have every way to quietly recuperate. But for the general public, whose lives depend on daily work, even if they know they have tuberculosis, how can they treat it? We know that people with lung disease are not necessarily those with ample means. On the contrary, those who are less well-off are more likely to suffer from lung disease. These poor people have already known from experience that they may have suspected lung disease, but because they have no money or time to treat it, they have to "leave it to fate." The disease gets worse day by day, but they still have to work. For people like this, even if there is a very low-cost opportunity for lung disease examination now, what will they do if they know they have lung disease? Therefore, we believe that it is not enough to just provide the general public with the opportunity to check for lung disease at any time at a low price. It does not mean that those suffering from lung disease can be saved. On the contrary, it only makes people know, adding infinite sorrow to them. This is indeed possible.

I do not have any doubts about this grand mass lung disease screening. On the contrary, we absolutely agree that this grand event is for the benefit of the general public. However, I also believe that in addition to providing low-cost examinations for citizens, it is best to take a further step and establish low-cost tuberculosis sanatoriums, or even free ones, so that the poor and needy can have a chance to be saved even if they suffer from lung disease. Only in this way can this mass screening be the most meaningful move.

We give the greatest praise to the Municipal Health Bureau and others for jointly organizing this mass tuberculosis screening. At the same time, we hope that after the screening, there will be even more meaningful events to further benefit the citizens.

The Story of the Melon

— Yunhai

These past few days of rain, it is said that the "wind wings" of the hurricane have passed through Shanghai, so we have eaten a lot of cheap watermelons. Yesterday, when the melon seller passed through the alley, it was still two small foreign coins each. Last night's wind dropped the price of melons to one small foreign coin each. I believe that if the weather does not turn hot, it will probably drop further. Speaking of this, I remembered a melon story from a few years ago.

At that time, I was living in the countryside. The melon garden next door belonged to my uncle from the same clan. He was a kind old man, and he treated us very well, taking care of us all day long: Don't steal melons, everyone will get a big slice when the melons are ripe in a few days. But we naughty children didn't listen to him. On a hazy moonlit night, we quietly went to the melon shed and picked one. Because we were still ignorant and naughty children, we were not very familiar with the nature of the melons. We accidentally picked one that was not yet ripe. When we ate it, it tasted a little sour. In a fit of anger, we threw the melon into the small river, and we mumbled and complained about our uncle, who was old and muddled and didn't grow sweet melons.

The next day, we heard our uncle scolding. He said angrily:

"You unconscionable melon thieves, you even steal the melons that I haven't even ripened yet, × your mother's rotten stuff!"

We felt as if we had been stung, and our hearts were filled with shame, but we still didn't dare to admit that we had done it. I still feel a little guilty about this matter.

The worst thing was that the old man not only didn't suspect us at all, but also told us very seriously when he finished telling us stories in the evening:

"When you grow up, don't be like this melon thief. You have no conscience! You pick it and it's not tasty, but you ruin other people's seeds. Isn't that bad for both sides?"

Hearing this kind of tone from this old man, even though we didn't understand anything, we almost cried. Especially, my heart was so sad that I wanted to tell the whole story. But in the end, we didn't confess to this poor old man, and this matter was buried in our little hearts.

Time passed quickly. The melons under the melon shed grew slowly. We watched our uncle call three brothers from the same clan to help him pick off some of the not very full and weak melons and carry them to the market in yokes to sell them to those who often went to the provincial city to sell "watermelon pickles." That night, the moonlight was very good, and we were sitting under the banyan tree enjoying the cool. The wrinkled face of our uncle was glowing with a soft light that we had never seen before.

After a while, he knocked off the ashes from his pipe and slowly said to us again (whatever he had in his heart, he would tell us a complete story).

"We're in luck this year. You say: watermelon pickles can also be sold at such a high price, so why worry about the melon cloth?"

He raised his head and smiled at the star-filled moonlit sky that had no rain clouds.

"Now they are eight-ripe. Just pass five days, - no: it's best to pass a few more days, so the melon will grow fat and big, and then we won't have to worry for half a year. What debt, tax, donation, nothing matters."

We didn't understand his words very much at that time, but we knew his happiness very well.

So, we sometimes went to the melon shed and stared at the melon with our eyes wide open, watching it grow fatter day by day. Later, the melons grew too heavy, and the melon shed seemed to be about to collapse. Our uncle put a lot of effort into tying the remaining "long melons" with bamboo cages to the melon shed, so that the poor melon shed would bear less weight.

The melons were all ripe. Old Wang, who often carried the melons to the market to sell them, told our uncle these days that it was time for the melons to be on the market, and that they shouldn't be too ripe or they wouldn't be sold. The stubborn uncle didn't listen to him. According to his experience, if he waited another day or two, the melons would definitely be sweeter and fuller. He, an old man, believed that this was never wrong.

However, this time it was beyond his expectations.

One day, the weather changed. In the evening, a storm swept in, and the rain followed, blowing and hitting the ground non-stop. The rain was so noisy that I couldn't sleep, and I spent a bored day at home with annoyance.

Finally, the rain stopped on the morning of the fifth day. I walked out early in the morning, and I was really surprised when I passed my uncle's melon shed. How come the melon shed had completely collapsed and the fat melons were crushed? So, I walked into the melon garden. Suddenly, it was as if I had stepped on something, and I was startled. When I saw that it was a person with protruding eyes lying there drenched in the rain, I screamed and walked out.

After coming out, I, who had always been timid, never talked to anyone about this matter.

Later, the village spread the word! My uncle had passed away.

Chen Junyang, named Yi Tong, is a famous modern seal carver, the younger brother of Ju Lai, and also a student of Mr. Zhao Shuru of Siming. He is assiduous in his studies, loves antiquity, and also engages in seal carving. He follows the Qin and Han dynasties, and his style is vigorous, lofty, and profound, in harmony with ancient meaning. Compared to those who imitate dilapidated styles and think of themselves as lofty and ancient, his style is very different. We reveal his recent works to show them to those who appreciate them. (Submission address: Xiling Seal Society, Wuma Road; Xuanhe Seal Society, Sanma Road)

Labor-Inducing Injection

— Li Ang

All kinds of medicine bottles were disorderly arranged on the table. A pair of small scissors and a clamp were especially sensitive to me. I wonder if my wife was lying on her back on the bed and saw me? She often mentioned these shiny iron instruments to me, and even said with a shudder: What if I have a difficult labor and have to use a knife? I always used comforting words to dispel her fears. At this time, I only hoped that she had her eyes closed. It was simply unreasonable to ask the female doctor not to take out the knife, clamp, and iron hook, unless we didn't ask them to come.

The narrow room was like a steamer in the summer. The stagnant air was filled with the smell of mineral medicines and my wife's intermittent moans. My wife's mother had prepared sweaters, skirts, warm water, bitter herb soup... everything, and was sitting next to the bed, murmuring prayers from time to time: "I hope my daughter will have a quick and easy birth... The child will come out quickly and wear new clothes..." The voice was restricted so low because she knew that I did not believe in gods and Buddhas. Two young female doctors were sitting by the window, fanning themselves and talking about idle things that had nothing to do with my wife's childbirth.

"Is it very painful now? Does it feel like you need to defecate?..." Sometimes, the older female doctor would turn her head and ask my wife once or twice, but my wife always shook her head slightly.

This made me anxious. I took out my watch several times. The doctor had been here for about two hours. I knew from the hospital regulations that the limit was four hours, and two dollars had to be added for each hour after that. It was common for childbirth to be delayed all day and all night, so how could we afford it? The more I thought about it, the more anxious I became. The doctor was still chatting leisurely, sometimes looking at the furniture in my room and the photo frames on the wall. At this time, my only hope was that my wife would shout loudly in pain, because urgent pain was the precursor to labor. I had learned this experience from the doctor. But how could I bear to see my wife suffer such severe pain! My wife's moan almost burst out from my heart... However, because of economic hardship... I had to have this contradictory hope. So, I looked at my watch again.

The female doctor, without waiting for me to speak, warned me as if to give me a warning: "I'm afraid it's going to be a difficult birth?"

"Difficult birth!" My wife turned her distressed face over: "Do... do... do I have to have surgery... I... I... can't stand it..." She stared at me with frightened and suspicious eyes. The female doctor laughed and explained to me:

"Her pain nerves are weak... She should be injected with a labor-inducing injection, four dollars per injection!"

Most of what she said were specialized terms in physiology and medicine. The only three sentences I could hear clearly were these. Four dollars per injection, wouldn't this extra expense exceed our budget again? Although we wouldn't be unable to pay this injection fee right now, the expenses after childbirth were constantly pouring in. My wife's dream of finding a job after childbirth had been completely shattered. Since my wife became pregnant, the relatives and friends who could help us had done their best. From now on, we would have to rely on our own weak sweat and strength to support this family that had added a member... Thinking about it, I expressed my opinion:

"Let's wait another half an hour. If there's no movement, then please give her the labor-inducing injection... But can the fee be reduced a little? I've already paid five dollars for the delivery."

"That's impossible. Our regulations are like this. Do you still cherish money when giving birth to a child!" They cast a pitying but somewhat disdainful glance at my wife. I squeezed my watch in my hand, as if I was squeezing my own heart. My wife was suffering from the torment of pain every minute. She frowned, she groaned, and she finally told her mother to ask the female doctor to give her the injection. She couldn't stand the pain any longer. My heart was also throbbing with pain. I bit my lip: "Okay, give her the labor-inducing injection." The female doctor happily prepared everything. In order to reduce my wife's suffering, I had to endure a little mental pain. Perhaps, it was necessary for me to endure this mental pain permanently, for the sake of future life, for the sake of future days...

Anticipation

— Already

For days, they had been anticipating the arrival of an unknowable hope. This hope was as if a hungry person sought food, or a desperate person prayed for divine help, it was so faint. However, living in hardship, they were sufficiently comforted for the moment by this hope. Every day, they dreamed, "If there were news saying I was accepted, how happy would I feel!"

But things often don't go as desired. The more eagerly they anticipated, the more disappointed they became. The postman came several times each day, but there was not a single letter for them. Yet, they did not abandon the hope they harbored in their hearts. Even after each disappointment, hope seemed even closer to realization, swirling in their minds. Because time passed quickly, they were getting closer to the hoped-for outcome.

"Why rush? It's only been three days; they probably haven't even looked at the exam papers yet." Initially, they always comforted themselves this way. They confidently predicted that it would take at least a week to mark the papers clearly. And after marking, they would need to make another decision on who to select. Recently, employers have been very cautious, and wouldn't act rashly. By the fourth, fifth, and sixth days, they each indulged in fantasies: "Maybe there will be a registered letter tomorrow?" But still, there was no news. Several "tomorrows" passed silently and without a sound.

At this point, they had to become anxious, even if they didn't want to! "How confident are you about your answers?" "That's hard to say. The composition is probably not bad; I wrote over two thousand words, and I was satisfied with it when I read it. But history and geography are a bit difficult; I only answered two-thirds of the twenty-odd questions, and some of them might be wrong. English was simple enough, passable. I forgot three or four words in one translation, but I don't think it will matter." "But there are so many applicants, seventy or eighty, and they're only taking two, passing might be difficult..." "That's for sure. Fifty dollars a month, who wouldn't compete for this job? I heard that those who took the exam that day had already been selected from a large pool; they received over six hundred letters of inquiry."

Thinking of the fifty-dollar reward, they really wished they could snatch the position immediately. Because they had been unemployed for so long, their desire for work was more urgent than others. But they couldn't do that; the only way was to leave it to fate. If they were lucky enough to be accepted, they would have temporary relief and wouldn't starve. If they were unlucky and failed, they would cry out in misery! The days ahead would be truly unmanageable; they had been living in poverty for months. However, after enduring many "winters," they said generously, "Forget it. If I fail, let others do it. The pain of unemployment is the same for everyone. We want to work, and of course, others want to work too."

Chen Jiazhen's Grand Funeral Yesterday

— Zhier

A funeral without female weeping Extremely miserable Will discuss burial issues Insufficient funds

Chen Jiazhen is dead!

His photography skills during his lifetime were praised by his peers, but he did not use them properly. He was once active in the film industry, and almost all of the covers and bathing suit photos of various film magazines were provided by him. He also compiled the Eight Great Stars collection, but his talent did not benefit the Chinese film industry in any way. If anything, it only made fans more infatuated with female stars, and further developed the distorted star system in a more distorted way.

However, his character and his treatment of friends were known for their honesty and sincerity. He always greeted people with a sincere smile, shaking hands firmly, and speaking without any slickness. From his Shaoxing-accented speech, one could immediately feel his sincerity.

Precisely because of his honesty and sincerity, he was deceived by two female stars (we are not feudal in saying that Yuan Diao must love Jia Gong, but using him, deceiving him with false love to elevate one's own position, this is always an ironclad fact). Because of this, his lung disease worsened, and he died suddenly at the age of only twenty-four.

After his death, the situation was very miserable. The words "desolate after death" are the most accurate description. As for the situation and the process, the newspapers have already recorded it, so I will omit it here. Now I just want to tell you some details of his grand funeral.

The mourning hall was very quiet, and very few friends arrived. Apart from a few friends from the New Fourth Circle, it could be said that there was almost no one. Among these fewer than twenty friends, this funeral without female weeping quietly let time slip by.

At 11:30, the grand funeral began. The fewer than twenty friends circled the coffin once, paying their last respects to him before the coffin was closed. Then, a very simple and unadorned memorial ceremony was held, presided over by Wu Liande, who offered three incense sticks and three libations. Then, the funeral procession immediately set off, and the coffin is now temporarily placed in Yongxi Hall (Shaoxing Guild Hall).

In terms of funeral gifts, Wu Liande, Hu Die, and Pan Yousheng jointly sent a white lotus flower basket; the Sanhe Publishing House sent a wreath; cash gifts included: Liangyou Company one hundred yuan, Hu Die and Pan Yousheng read out the yuan, Yuan Shude ten yuan, Yuan Meiyun ten yuan (this was brought by Yuan Shude, but the envelope was written with "Yuan Meiyun's mother"). There were also several other ten yuan gifts, and Gao Jilin, Cui Wanqiu, Tang Na, Tang Yu, etc., each gave two yuan.

The female stars whose photos Chen Jiazhen had taken a lot of during his lifetime, none of them came, nor were there any "funeral gifts." This made people think of the old saying that people matter when they are alive, and human relationships are as thin as paper. A friend said that if Chen Jiazhen had taken them somewhere with his camera equipment to take pictures, they would definitely have followed. But unfortunately, Jiazhen is dead.

Attached is a message: Yuan Meiyun performed "Empress He Scolds the Court" on stage at Yan Mansion's private performance last night (the 17th). As for Diao Gong Ban Hua, she is said to be in Suzhou. At the same time, Ke Ni "er," the former "Daily Film" "film critic" who had never even sat on her bed, is also said to be in Suzhou.

Finally, a message was received from Chen Jiazhen's funeral committee that Ma Guoliang, Lin Zecang, Cui Wanqiu, Jiang Donglai, and Zhong Xinru have been appointed as funeral committee members. They will hold one or two meetings to discuss burial issues. Furthermore, the funds are still greatly insufficient. The mailing address is on the second floor of No. 138 Nanjing Road. If friends have any donations, they can send them directly to that address to obtain a receipt. All accounts will also be published successively.

Margaret Lindsay in "Wife of the Mountain Stronghold"
